             <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="340" data-file-width="512" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Flag_of_the_Valencian_Community_%282x3%29.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Valencian_Community_%282x3%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Flag_of_the_Valencian_Community_%282x3%29.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Valencian_Community_%282x3%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/16/Flag_of_the_Valencian_Community_%282x3%29.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_Valencian_Community_%282x3%29.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
            </span>
            <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">
             Valencian Community
            </a>
            (as Valencian)
           </li>
          </ul>
         </div>
         <br/>

      <p>
       <b>
        Catalan
       </b>
       (
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'k' in 'kind'">
            k
           </span>
           <span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">
            æ
           </span>
           <span title="'t' in 'tie'">
            t
           </span>
           <span title="/əl/: 'le' in 'bottle'">
            əl
           </span>
           <span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">
            æ
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
          </span>
          , -
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
          </span>
          ,
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˌ/: secondary stress follows">
            ˌ
           </span>
           <span title="'k' in 'kind'">
            k
           </span>
           <span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">
            æ
           </span>
           <span title="'t' in 'tie'">
            t
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'l' in 'lie'">
            l
           </span>
           <span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">
            æ
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       ;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dictionary.reference.com_4-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-dictionary.reference.com-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endonym" title="Endonym">
        autonym
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        català
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Catalan" title="Help:IPA/Catalan">
         [kətəˈla]
        </a>
       </span>
       <small>
        or
       </small>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Catalan" title="Help:IPA/Catalan">
         [kataˈla]
        </a>
       </span>
       ) is a
       <a href="/wiki/Western_Romance_languages" title="Western Romance languages">
        Western Romance language
       </a>
       derived from
       <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">
        Vulgar Latin
       </a>
       (i.e. the spoken language of the people in common use) and named after the medieval
       <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Catalonia" title="Principality of Catalonia">
        Principality of Catalonia
       </a>
       , in northeastern modern
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       . It is the only official language of
       <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">
        Andorra
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010191_5-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010191-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and a co-official language of the Spanish
       <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_communities_of_Spain" title="Autonomous communities of Spain">
        autonomous communities
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">
        Catalonia
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">
        Balearic Islands
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">
        Valencia
       </a>
       (where the language is known as
       <a href="/wiki/Valencian" title="Valencian">
        Valencian
       </a>
       ). It also has semi-official status in the
       <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">
        Italian
       </a>
       commune of
       <a href="/wiki/Alghero" title="Alghero">
        Alghero
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These territories are often called
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_Countries" title="Catalan Countries">
        Catalan Countries
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Catalan evolved from Vulgar Latin in the Middle Ages around the eastern
       <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">
        Pyrenees
       </a>
       . 19th-century Spain saw a
       <a href="/wiki/Renaixen%C3%A7a" title="Renaixença">
        Catalan literary revival
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010190–191_7-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010190–191-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates20096–7_8-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates20096–7-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       culminating in the early 1900s.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

         <a href="#Geographic_distribution">
          <span class="tocnumber">
           4
          </span>
          <span class="toctext">
           Geographic distribution
          </span>
         </a>
         <ul>
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11">
           <a href="#Catalan-speaking_territories">
            <span class="tocnumber">
             4.1
            </span>
            <span class="toctext">
             Catalan-speaking territories

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_and_pronunciation">
        Etymology and pronunciation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology and pronunciation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Catalonia#Etymology_and_pronunciation" title="Catalonia">
        Catalonia § Etymology and pronunciation
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:244px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Extensi%C3%B3_de_la_llengua_catalana_als_Pa%C3%AFsos_Catalans.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1125" data-file-width="1500" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Extensi%C3%B3_de_la_llengua_catalana_als_Pa%C3%AFsos_Catalans.png/242px-Extensi%C3%B3_de_la_llengua_catalana_als_Pa%C3%AFsos_Catalans.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Extensi%C3%B3_de_la_llengua_catalana_als_Pa%C3%AFsos_Catalans.png/363px-Extensi%C3%B3_de_la_llengua_catalana_als_Pa%C3%AFsos_Catalans.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Extensi%C3%B3_de_la_llengua_catalana_als_Pa%C3%AFsos_Catalans.png/484px-Extensi%C3%B3_de_la_llengua_catalana_als_Pa%C3%AFsos_Catalans.png 2x" width="242"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Extensi%C3%B3_de_la_llengua_catalana_als_Pa%C3%AFsos_Catalans.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <b>
          <a href="/wiki/Catalan_Countries" title="Catalan Countries">
           Catalan Countries
          </a>
         </b>
         <i>
          (
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pa%C3%AFsos_Catalans" title="Països Catalans">
           Països Catalans
          </a>
          ):
         </i>
         (In orange, strict Catalan-speaking area) NE modern
         <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
          Spain
         </a>
         (
         <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">
          Catalonia
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">
          Valencian Community
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">
          Balearic Islands
         </a>
         ), SE.
         <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
          France
         </a>
         (
         <a href="/wiki/Roussillon" title="Roussillon">
          Roussillon
         </a>
         , touching the
         <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">
          Pyrenees
         </a>
         ) and Comune of Alghero (NW coast of
         <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">
          Sardinia
         </a>
         , Island belonging to
         <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">
          Italy
         </a>
         )
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:241px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aragonese_Empire_1443.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="255" data-file-width="386" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Aragonese_Empire_1443.svg/239px-Aragonese_Empire_1443.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Aragonese_Empire_1443.svg/359px-Aragonese_Empire_1443.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Aragonese_Empire_1443.svg/478px-Aragonese_Empire_1443.svg.png 2x" width="239"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aragonese_Empire_1443.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Aragon" title="Crown of Aragon">
          Crown of Aragon
         </a>
         in 1443. King
         <a href="/wiki/James_I_of_Aragon" title="James I of Aragon">
          James the Conqueror
         </a>
         [1208-1276] dictated his autobiographical chronicles entirely in Catalan. Much of this territory nowadays makes up the
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Catalan_Countries" title="Catalan Countries">
           Catalan Countries
          </a>
          .
         </i>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The word
       <i>
        Catalan
       </i>
       derives from the territory of
       <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">
        Catalonia
       </a>
       , itself of disputed etymology. The main theory suggests that
       <i>
        Catalunya
       </i>
       (
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_language" title="Latin language">
        Latin
       </a>
       <i>
        Gathia Launia
       </i>
       ) derives from the name
       <i>
        Gothia
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        Gauthia
       </i>
       ("Land of the Goths"), since the origins of the Catalan counts, lords and people were found in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/March_of_Gothia" title="March of Gothia">
        March of Gothia
       </a>
       , whence
       <i>
        Gothland
       </i>
       &gt;
       <i>
        Gothlandia
       </i>
       &gt;
       <i>
        Gothalania
       </i>
       &gt;
       <i>
        Catalonia
       </i>
       theoretically derived.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGarcía_Venero2006_9-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGarcía_Venero2006-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBurke1900154_10-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBurke1900154-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">
        English
       </a>
       , the term referring to a person first appears in the mid 14th century as
       <i>
        Catelaner
       </i>
       , followed in the 15th century as
       <i>
        Catellain
       </i>
       (from
       <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">
        French
       </a>
       ). It is attested a language name since at least 1652.
       <i>
        Catalan
       </i>
       can be pronounced as
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'k' in 'kind'">
            k
           </span>
           <span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">
            æ
           </span>
           <span title="'t' in 'tie'">
            t
           </span>
           <span title="/əl/: 'le' in 'bottle'">
            əl
           </span>
           <span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">
            æ
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="'k' in 'kind'">
            k
           </span>
           <span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">
            æ
           </span>
           <span title="'t' in 'tie'">
            t
           </span>
           <span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">
            ə
           </span>
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'l' in 'lie'">
            l
           </span>
           <span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">
            æ
           </span>
           <span title="'n' in 'nigh'">
            n
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       or
       <span class="nowrap">
        <span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt">
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">
          /
          <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted">
           <span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">
            ˈ
           </span>
           <span title="'k' in 'kind'">
            k
           </span>
           <span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">
            æ
           </span>
           <span title="'t' in 'tie'">
            t
           </span>
           <span title="/əl/: 'le' in 'bottle'">
            əl
           </span>
           <span title="/ən/: 'on' in 'button'">
            ən
           </span>
          </span>
          /
         </a>
        </span>
       </span>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dictionary.reference.com_4-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-dictionary.reference.com-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endonym" title="Endonym">
        endonym
       </a>
       is pronounced
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /kə.təˈɫa/
       </span>
       in the Eastern Catalan dialects, and
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ka.taˈɫa/
       </span>
       in the Western dialects. In the
       <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">
        Valencian Community
       </a>
       , the term
       <i>
        valencià
       </i>
       (
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /va.len.siˈa/
       </span>
       ) is frequently used instead. The names "Catalan" and "Valencian" are two names for the same language.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELledó2011334–337_11-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELledó2011334–337-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dictalmen_AVL_12-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-dictalmen_AVL-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Cleanup" title="Wikipedia:Cleanup">
          <span title="The section on Catalan-speaking territories says that Valencian is the name for the variety spoken in Valencia, not for the language spoken in other regions, such as Catalonia and the Balearic Islands. (January 2018)">
           inconsistent
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       See also
       <a href="#About_Valencian">
        status of Valencian
       </a>
       below.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">

       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">

        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">

          </a>
         </div>
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Homilies_d%27Organy%C3%A0" title="Homilies d'Organyà">
           Homilies d'Organyà
          </a>
         </i>
         (12th century)
        </div>

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:194px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Greuges_de_Guitard_Isarn.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="255" data-file-width="286" height="171" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Greuges_de_Guitard_Isarn.jpg/192px-Greuges_de_Guitard_Isarn.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/04/Greuges_de_Guitard_Isarn.jpg 1.5x" width="192"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Greuges_de_Guitard_Isarn.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Fragment of the
         <i>
          <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Greuges_de_Guitard_Isarn&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Greuges de Guitard Isarn (page does not exist)">
           Greuges de Guitard Isarn
          </a>
         </i>
         (ca. 1080–1095), one of the earliest texts written almost completely in Catalan,
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVeny19979–18_13-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVeny19979–18-13">
           [13]
          </a>
         </sup>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoran200437–38_14-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoran200437–38-14">
           [14]
          </a>
         </sup>
         predating the famous
         <i>
          <a href="/wiki/Homilies_d%27Organy%C3%A0" title="Homilies d'Organyà">
           Homilies d'Organyà
          </a>
         </i>
         by a century
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif">
         <img alt="Linguistic map Southwestern Europe.gif" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="544" data-file-width="600" height="218" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif/240px-Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif/360px-Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif/480px-Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif 2x" width="240"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Linguistic_map_Southwestern_Europe.gif" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">
        Middle Ages
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Old_Catalan" title="Old Catalan">
        Old Catalan
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Phonological_history_of_Catalan" title="Phonological history of Catalan">
        Phonological history of Catalan
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       By the 9th century, Catalan had evolved from
       <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">
        Vulgar Latin
       </a>
       on both sides of the eastern end of the
       <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">
        Pyrenees
       </a>
       , as well as the territories of the Roman province of
       <a href="/wiki/Hispania_Tarraconensis" title="Hispania Tarraconensis">
        Hispania Tarraconensis
       </a>
       to the south.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates6–7_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates6–7-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       From the 8th century onwards the Catalan counts extended their territory southwards and westwards at the expense of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">
        Muslims
       </a>
       , bringing their language with them.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates6–7_15-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates6–7-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This process was given definitive impetus with the separation of the
       <a href="/wiki/County_of_Barcelona" title="County of Barcelona">
        County of Barcelona
       </a>
       from the
       <a href="/wiki/Carolingian_Empire" title="Carolingian Empire">
        Carolingian Empire
       </a>
       in 988.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates20096–7_8-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates20096–7-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the 11th century, documents written in
       <a href="/wiki/Macaronic_language" title="Macaronic language">
        macaronic Latin
       </a>
       begin to show Catalan elements,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoran200437–38_14-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoran200437–38-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       with texts written almost completely in Romance appearing by 1080.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoran200437–38_14-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoran200437–38-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Old Catalan shared many features with
       <a href="/wiki/Gallo-Romance_languages" title="Gallo-Romance languages">
        Gallo-Romance
       </a>
       , diverging from
       <a href="/wiki/Old_Occitan" title="Old Occitan">
        Old Occitan
       </a>
       between the 11th and 14th centuries.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERiquer1964_16-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERiquer1964-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       During the 11th and 12th centuries the Catalan rulers expanded up to north of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ebro_river" title="Ebro river">
        Ebro river
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates6–7_15-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates6–7-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and in the 13th century they conquered the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Valencia" title="Kingdom of Valencia">
        Land of Valencia
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Balearic_Islands" title="Balearic Islands">
        Balearic Islands
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates20096–7_8-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates20096–7-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The city of
       <a href="/wiki/Alghero" title="Alghero">
        Alghero
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Sardinia" title="Sardinia">
        Sardinia
       </a>
       was repopulated with Catalan speakers in the 14th century. The language also reached
       <a href="/wiki/Murcia" title="Murcia">
        Murcia
       </a>
       , which became Spanish-speaking in the 15th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010190_17-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010190-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Low_Middle_Ages" title="Low Middle Ages">
        Low Middle Ages
       </a>
       , Catalan went through a golden age, reaching a peak of maturity and cultural richness.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates6–7_15-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates6–7-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Examples include the work of Majorcan polymath
       <a href="/wiki/Ramon_Llull" title="Ramon Llull">
        Ramon Llull
       </a>
       (1232–1315), the Four Great Chronicles (13th–14th centuries), and the Valencian school of poetry culminating in
       <a href="/wiki/Ausi%C3%A0s_March" title="Ausiàs March">
        Ausiàs March
       </a>
       (1397–1459).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates6–7_15-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates6–7-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By the 15th century, the city of
       <a href="/wiki/Valencia" title="Valencia">
        Valencia
       </a>
       had become the sociocultural center of the
       <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Aragon" title="Crown of Aragon">
        Crown of Aragon
       </a>
       , and Catalan was present all over the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mediterranean" title="Mediterranean">
        Mediterranean
       </a>
       world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates6–7_15-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates6–7-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       During this period, the Royal Chancery propagated a highly standardized language.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates6–7_15-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates6–7-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Catalan was widely used as an official language in Sicily until the 15th century, and in Sardinia until the 17th.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010190_17-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010190-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       During this period, the language was what Costa Carreras terms "one of the 'great languages' of medieval Europe".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates20096–7_8-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates20096–7-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Joanot_Martorell" title="Joanot Martorell">
        Martorell
       </a>
       's outstanding
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates6–7_15-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates6–7-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       novel of chivalry
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tirant_lo_Blanc" title="Tirant lo Blanc">
         Tirant lo Blanc
        </a>
       </i>
       (1490) shows a transition from Medieval to Renaissance values, something that can also be seen in
       <a href="/wiki/Bernat_Metge" title="Bernat Metge">
        Metge
       </a>
       's work.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates6–7_15-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates6–7-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The first book produced with movable type in the
       <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">
        Iberian Peninsula
       </a>
       was printed in Catalan.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates20096–7_8-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates20096–7-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Start_of_the_modern_era">
        Start of the modern era
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Start of the modern era">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       With the union of the crowns of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Castille" title="Kingdom of Castille">
        Castille
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Aragon" title="Crown of Aragon">
        Aragon
       </a>
       (1479), the use of
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       gradually became more prestigious
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010190_17-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010190-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and marked the start of the decline of the Catalan.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates20096–7_8-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates20096–7-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010190–191_7-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010190–191-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Starting in the 16th century, Catalan literature came under the influence of Spanish, and the urban and literary classes became
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bilingualism" title="Bilingualism">
        bilingual
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010190_17-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010190-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       With the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_the_Pyrenees" title="Treaty of the Pyrenees">
        Treaty of the Pyrenees
       </a>
       (1659),
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       ceded the
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Catalonia" title="Northern Catalonia">
        northern part of Catalonia
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
        France
       </a>
       , and soon thereafter the
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Catalan" title="Northern Catalan">
        local Catalan varieties
       </a>
       came under the influence of
       <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">
        French
       </a>
       , which in 1700 became the sole official language of the region.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010191_5-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010191-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Shortly after the
       <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">
        French Revolution
       </a>
       (1789), the
       <a href="/wiki/French_First_Republic" title="French First Republic">
        French First Republic
       </a>
       prohibited official use of, and enacted discriminating policies against, the regional languages of France, such as Catalan,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alsatian_language" title="Alsatian language">
        Alsatian
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Breton_language" title="Breton language">
        Breton
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Occitan_language" title="Occitan language">
        Occitan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Flemish" title="Flemish">
        Flemish
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">
        Basque
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="French_state:_19th_to_20th_centuries">
        French state: 19th to 20th centuries
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: French state: 19th to 20th centuries">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:189px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Interdiction_officielle_de_la_langue_catalana_2_avril_1700.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1374" data-file-width="1030" height="249" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Interdiction_officielle_de_la_langue_catalana_2_avril_1700.jpg/187px-Interdiction_officielle_de_la_langue_catalana_2_avril_1700.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Interdiction_officielle_de_la_langue_catalana_2_avril_1700.jpg/280px-Interdiction_officielle_de_la_langue_catalana_2_avril_1700.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Interdiction_officielle_de_la_langue_catalana_2_avril_1700.jpg/373px-Interdiction_officielle_de_la_langue_catalana_2_avril_1700.jpg 2x" width="187"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Interdiction_officielle_de_la_langue_catalana_2_avril_1700.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Official Decree Prohibiting the Catalan Language in France
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:190px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SpeakFrenchBeClean.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1072" data-file-width="1430" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/SpeakFrenchBeClean.jpg/188px-SpeakFrenchBeClean.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/SpeakFrenchBeClean.jpg/282px-SpeakFrenchBeClean.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/SpeakFrenchBeClean.jpg/376px-SpeakFrenchBeClean.jpg 2x" width="188"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SpeakFrenchBeClean.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         "Speak French, be clean", school wall in
         <a href="/wiki/Ayguat%C3%A9bia-Talau" title="Ayguatébia-Talau">
          Ayguatébia-Talau
         </a>
         , 2010
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Language_policy_in_France" title="Language policy in France">
        Language policy in France
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Vergonha" title="Vergonha">
        Vergonha
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Patois" title="Patois">
        Patois
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Following the French capture of
       <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">
        Algeria
       </a>
       (1833), that region saw several waves of Catalan-speaking settlers. People from the Spanish
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alacant" title="Alacant">
        Alacant
       </a>
       province settled around
       <a href="/wiki/Oran" title="Oran">
        Oran
       </a>
       , whereas
       <a href="/wiki/Algiers" title="Algiers">
        Algiers
       </a>
       received immigration from
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Catalonia" title="Northern Catalonia">
        Northern Catalonia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Menorca" title="Menorca">
        Menorca
       </a>
       . Their speech was known as
       <i>
        patuet
       </i>
       . By 1911, the number of Catalan speakers was around 100,000. After the declaration of independence of Algeria in 1962, almost all the Catalan speakers fled to Northern Catalonia (as
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pieds-Noirs" title="Pieds-Noirs">
         Pieds-Noirs
        </a>
       </i>
       ) or Alacant.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMarfany2002_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMarfany2002-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Nowadays, France recognizes only French as an official language. Nevertheless, on 10 December 2007, the
       <a href="/wiki/General_Council_of_the_Pyr%C3%A9n%C3%A9es-Orientales" title="General Council of the Pyrénées-Orientales">
        General Council of the Pyrénées-Orientales
       </a>
       officially recognized Catalan as one of the languages of the department
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charte_en_faveur_du_Catalan_21-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Charte_en_faveur_du_Catalan-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and seeks to further promote it in public life and education.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Spanish_state:_18th_to_20th_centuries">
        Spanish state: 18th to 20th centuries
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Spanish state: 18th to 20th centuries">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Nueva_Planta_decrees" title="Nueva Planta decrees">
        Nueva Planta decrees
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Language_politics_in_Spain_under_Franco" title="Language politics in Spain under Franco">
        Language politics in Spain under Franco
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Anti-Catalanism" title="Anti-Catalanism">
        Anti-Catalanism
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The decline of Catalan continued in the 16th and 17th centuries. The defeat of the pro-Habsburg coalition in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_of_Spanish_Succession" title="War of Spanish Succession">
        War of Spanish Succession
       </a>
       (1714) initiated a series of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nueva_planta_decrees" title="Nueva planta decrees">
        laws
       </a>
       which, among other centralizing measures, imposed the use of
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       in legal documentation all over Spain.
      </p>
      <p>
       In parallel, however, the 19th century saw a Catalan literary revival (
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Renaixen%C3%A7a" title="Renaixença">
         Renaixença
        </a>
       </i>
       ), which has continued up to the present day.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010191_5-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010191-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This period starts with
       <a href="/wiki/Bonaventura_Carles_Aribau" title="Bonaventura Carles Aribau">
        Aribau
       </a>
       's
       <i>
        Ode to the Homeland
       </i>
       (1833); followed in the second half of the 19th century, and the early 20th by the work of
       <a href="/wiki/Jacint_Verdaguer" title="Jacint Verdaguer">
        Verdaguer
       </a>
       (poetry),
       <a href="/wiki/Narc%C3%ADs_Oller" title="Narcís Oller">
        Oller
       </a>
       (realist novel), and
       <a href="/wiki/%C3%80ngel_Guimer%C3%A0" title="Àngel Guimerà">
        Guimerà
       </a>
       (drama).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECosta_Carreras200710–11_22-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECosta_Carreras200710–11-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the 19th century, the region of
       <a href="/wiki/Carche" title="Carche">
        Carche
       </a>
       , in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Province_of_Murcia" title="Province of Murcia">
        province of Murcia
       </a>
       was repopulated with Catalan speakers from the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Land_of_Valencia" title="Land of Valencia">
        Land of Valencia
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler20051_23-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler20051-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Second_Spanish_Republic" title="Second Spanish Republic">
        Second Spanish Republic
       </a>
       (1931–1939) saw a brief period of tolerance, with most restrictions against Catalan being lifted.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010191_5-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010191-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Despite orthographic standardization in 1913 and the official status of the language during the
       <a href="/wiki/Second_Spanish_Republic" title="Second Spanish Republic">
        Second Spanish Republic
       </a>
       (1931–39) the
       <a href="/wiki/Francoist_Spain" title="Francoist Spain">
        Francoist dictatorship
       </a>
       banned the use of Catalan in schools and in the public administration between 1939 and 1975.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010190–191_7-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010190–191-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Present_day">
        Present day
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Present day">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Since the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_transition_to_democracy" title="Spanish transition to democracy">
        Spanish transition to democracy
       </a>
       (1975–1982), Catalan has been institutionalizated as an official language, language of education, and language of mass media; all of which have contributed to its increased prestige.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler2003207_25-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler2003207-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">
        Catalonia
       </a>
       , there is an unparalleled large
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bilingualism" title="Bilingualism">
        bilingual
       </a>
       European
       <a href="/wiki/Stateless_nation" title="Stateless nation">
        non-state
       </a>
       speech community.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler2003207_25-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler2003207-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The teaching of Catalan is mandatory in all schools,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010191_5-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010191-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but it is possible to use Spanish for studying in the public education system of Catalonia in two situations – if the teacher assigned to a class chooses to use Spanish, or during the learning process of one or more recently arrived immigrant students.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There is also some intergenerational shift towards Catalan.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010191_5-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010191-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to the
       <a href="/wiki/Statistical_Institute_of_Catalonia" title="Statistical Institute of Catalonia">
        Statistical Institute of Catalonia
       </a>
       , in 2013 the Catalan language is the second most commonly used in Catalonia, after
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       , as a native or self-defining language: 7% of the population self-identifies with both Catalan and Spanish equally, 36.4% with Catalan and 47.5% only Spanish.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-idescat.cat_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-idescat.cat-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2003 the same studies concluded no language preference for self-identification within the population above 15 years old: 5% self-identified with both languages, 44.3% with Catalan and 47.5 with Spanish.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In order to promote use of Catalan, the
       <a href="/wiki/Generalitat_de_Catalunya" title="Generalitat de Catalunya">
        Generalitat de Catalunya
       </a>
       (Catalonia's official Autonomous government) spends part of its annual budget on the promotion of the use of Catalan in Catalonia and in other territories.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Andorra" title="Andorra">
        Andorra
       </a>
       , Catalan has always been the sole official language.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010191_5-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010191-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Since the promulgation of the
       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Andorra" title="Constitution of Andorra">
        1993 constitution
       </a>
       , several policies favouring Catalan have been enforced, like Catalan medium education.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010191_5-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010191-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On the other hand, there are several
       <a href="/wiki/Language_shift" title="Language shift">
        language shift
       </a>
       processes currently taking place. In the
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Catalonia" title="Northern Catalonia">
        Northern Catalonia
       </a>
       area of France, Catalan has followed the same trend as the other minority languages of France, with most of its native speakers being 60 or older (as of 2004).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010191_5-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010191-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Catalan is studied as a foreign language by 30% of the primary education students, and by 15% of the secondary.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010191_5-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010191-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The cultural association
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/La_Bressola" title="La Bressola">
         La Bressola
        </a>
       </i>
       promotes a network of community-run schools engaged in Catalan language immersion programs.
      </p>
      <p>
       In
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alicante_province" title="Alicante province">
        Alicante province
       </a>
       Catalan is being replaced by
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       , and in
       <a href="/wiki/Alghero" title="Alghero">
        Alghero
       </a>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">
        Italian
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler2003207_25-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler2003207-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are also well ingrained
       <a href="/wiki/Diglossia" title="Diglossia">
        diglossic
       </a>
       attitudes against Catalan in the
       <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">
        Valencian Community
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ibiza" title="Ibiza">
        Ibiza
       </a>
       , and to a lesser extent, in the rest of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balearic_islands" title="Balearic islands">
        Balearic islands
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010191_5-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler2010191-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Classification_and_relationship_with_other_Romance_languages">
        Classification and relationship with other Romance languages
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Classification and relationship with other Romance languages">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:190px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Romance-lg-classification-en.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="556" data-file-width="1011" height="103" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Romance-lg-classification-en.svg/188px-Romance-lg-classification-en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Romance-lg-classification-en.svg/282px-Romance-lg-classification-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Romance-lg-classification-en.svg/376px-Romance-lg-classification-en.svg.png 2x" width="188"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Romance-lg-classification-en.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Chart of Romance languages based on structural and comparative criteria (not on socio-functional ones). Koryakov (2001) includes Catalan in
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Occitano-Romance" title="Occitano-Romance">
          Occitano-Romance
         </a>
         , distinct from
         <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Romance_languages" title="Iberian Romance languages">
          Iberian Romance
         </a>
         .
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKoryakov2001_30-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKoryakov2001-30">
           [30]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The ascription of Catalan to the
       <a href="/wiki/Occitano-Romance_languages" title="Occitano-Romance languages">
        Occitano-Romance
       </a>
       branch of
       <a href="/wiki/Gallo-Romance_languages" title="Gallo-Romance languages">
        Gallo-Romance languages
       </a>
       is not shared by all linguists and philologists, particularly among Spanish ones, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Ram%C3%B3n_Men%C3%A9ndez_Pidal" title="Ramón Menéndez Pidal">
        Ramón Menéndez Pidal
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       According to
       <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Bec" title="Pierre Bec">
        Pèire Bèc
       </a>
       , its specific classification is as follows:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">
         Romance languages
        </a>
        <ul>
         <li>
          <a href="/wiki/Italo-Western_languages" title="Italo-Western languages">
           Italo-Western languages
          </a>
          <ul>
           <li>
            <a href="/wiki/Western_Romance_languages" title="Western Romance languages">
             Western Romance languages
            </a>
            <ul>
             <li>
              <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gallo-Iberian_languages" title="Gallo-Iberian languages">
               Gallo-Iberian languages
              </a>
              <ul>
               <li>
                <a href="/wiki/Gallo-Romance_languages" title="Gallo-Romance languages">
                 Gallo-Romance languages
                </a>
                (alternatively classified as
                <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Romance_languages" title="Iberian Romance languages">
                 Iberian Romance language
                </a>
                )
                <ul>
                 <li>
                  <a href="/wiki/Occitano-Romance_languages" title="Occitano-Romance languages">
                   Occitano-Romance languages
                  </a>
                  (alternatively classified as
                  <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Romance_languages#Family_tree" title="Iberian Romance languages">
                   East Iberian language
                  </a>
                  )
                  <ul>
                   <li>
                    Catalan language
                   </li>
                  </ul>
                 </li>
                </ul>
               </li>
              </ul>
             </li>
            </ul>
           </li>
          </ul>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Catalan bears varying degrees of similarity to the linguistic varieties subsumed under the cover term
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Occitan_language" title="Occitan language">
         Occitan language
        </a>
       </i>
       (see also
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Occitan#Differences_between_Occitan_and_Catalan" title="Occitan">
        differences between Occitan and Catalan
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Gallo-Romance_languages" title="Gallo-Romance languages">
        Gallo-Romance languages
       </a>
       ). Thus, as it should be expected from closely related languages, Catalan today shares many traits with other Romance languages.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Relationship_with_other_Romance_languages">
        Relationship with other Romance languages
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Relationship with other Romance languages">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Catalan shares many traits with the other neighboring
       <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">
        Romance languages
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">
        Italian
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sardinian_language" title="Sardinian language">
        Sardinian
       </a>
       , Occitan, and Spanish).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler20051_23-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler20051-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, despite being spoken mostly on the
       <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">
        Iberian Peninsula
       </a>
       , Catalan has marked differences with the
       <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Romance_languages" title="Iberian Romance languages">
        Iberian Romance
       </a>
       group (
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       ) in terms of
       <a href="/wiki/Pronunciation" title="Pronunciation">
        pronunciation
       </a>
       , grammar, and especially vocabulary; showing instead its closest affinity with
       <a href="/wiki/Occitan_language" title="Occitan language">
        Occitan
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632_31-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20104_32-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20104-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchlösser200560f_33-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchlösser200560f-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and to a lesser extent
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gallo-Romance" title="Gallo-Romance">
        Gallo-Romance
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">
        French
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Franco-Proven%C3%A7al_language" title="Franco-Provençal language">
        Franco-Provençal
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gallo-Italian_languages" title="Gallo-Italian languages">
        Gallo-Italian
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:11_34-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-:11-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJud1925_35-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJud1925-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColón199333–35_36-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColón199333–35-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoll195847_37-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoll195847-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632_31-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20104_32-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20104-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchlösser200560f_33-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchlösser200560f-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       According to
       <a href="/wiki/Ethnologue" title="Ethnologue">
        Ethnologue
       </a>
       , the lexical similarity between Catalan and other Romance languages is: 87% with Italian; 85% with Portuguese and Spanish; 76% with
       <a href="/wiki/Ladin_language" title="Ladin language">
        Ladin
       </a>
       ; 75% with Sardinian; and 73% with Romanian.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-e18_38-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-e18-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable" style="margin:auto; text-align:center;">
       <caption>
        <b>
         Lexical comparison of 24 words among Western Romance languages:
         <br/>
         17 cognates with Gallo-Romance, 5
         <a href="/wiki/Isogloss" title="Isogloss">
          isoglosses
         </a>
         with Iberian Romance, 3 isoglosses with Occitan, and 1 unique word.
        </b>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEJud1925_35-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEJud1925-35">
          [35]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColón199333–35_36-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColón199333–35-36">
          [36]
         </a>

          papar
         </i>
         in slang),
         <i>
          <b>
           manjar
          </b>
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          <b>
           a mânca
          </b>
         </i>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <table class="wikitable" style="margin:auto; text-align:center;">
       <caption>
        Catalan and Spanish cognates with different meanings
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoll195847_37-1">

         </a>
        </sup>
       </caption>
       <tr>
        <th>
         <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">

         </a>
        </th>

        </th>

         </a>
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
          accostare
         </span>
        </td>

         "to bring closer"
        </td>

        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>

         </i>

         <br/>
         wake up"
        </td>

         </i>
        </td>

        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">

         </span>

         </i>

        </td>

        </td>
       </tr>

         </span>

         </i>
        </td>

         "to search"
        </td>

         </i>

        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">

         </span>

        </td>

         </i>

        </td>
       </tr>

         </i>
        </td>

         "wife"
        </td>

         <i>
          mujer
         </i>
        </td>

         "woman or wife"
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       During much of its history, and especially during the
       <a href="/wiki/Francoist_Spain" title="Francoist Spain">
        Francoist dictatorship
       </a>
       (1939–1975), the Catalan language was ridiculed as a mere dialect of
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20104_32-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20104-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchlösser200560f_33-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchlösser200560f-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This view, based on political and ideological considerations, has no linguistic validity.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20104_32-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20104-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchlösser200560f_33-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchlösser200560f-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Spanish and Catalan have important differences in their sound systems, lexicon, and grammatical features, placing the language in features closer to
       <a href="/wiki/Occitan_language" title="Occitan language">
        Occitan
       </a>
       (and
       <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">
        French
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20104_32-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20104-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESchlösser200560f_33-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESchlösser200560f-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       There is evidence that, at least from the 2nd century
       <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
        a.d.
       </span>
       , the vocabulary and phonology of Roman
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tarraconensis" title="Tarraconensis">
        Tarraconensis
       </a>
       was different from the rest of Roman Hispania.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632_31-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Differentiation arose generally because Spanish,
       <a href="/wiki/Asturian_language" title="Asturian language">
        Asturian
       </a>
       , and Galician-Portuguese share certain peripheral archaisms (Spanish
       <i>
        hervir
       </i>
       , Asturian/Portuguese
       <i>
        ferver
       </i>
       vs. Catalan
       <i>
        bullir
       </i>
       , Occitan
       <i>
        bolir
       </i>
       "to boil") and innovatory regionalisms (Sp
       <i>
        novillo
       </i>
       , Ast
       <i>
        nuviellu
       </i>
       vs. Cat
       <i>
        torell
       </i>
       , Oc
       <i>
        taurèl
       </i>
       "bullock"), while Catalan has a shared history with the Western Romance innovative core, especially Occitan.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColón199355_43-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColón199355-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632_31-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Like all Romance languages, Catalan has a handful of native words which are rare or only found in Catalan. These include:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        verbs:
        <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
         cōnfīgere
        </span>
        ‘to fasten; transfix’ &gt;
        <i>
         confegir
        </i>
        ‘to compose, write up’,
        <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
         congemināre
        </span>
        &gt;
        <i>
         conjuminar
        </i>
        ‘to combine, conjugate’,
        <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
         de-ex-somnitare
        </span>
        &gt;
        <i>
         deixondar/-ir
        </i>
        ‘to wake; awaken’,
        <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
         dēnsāre
        </span>
        ‘to thicken; crowd together’ &gt;
        <i>
         desar
        </i>
        ‘to save, keep’,
        <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
         īgnōrāre
        </span>
        &gt;
        <i>
         enyorar
        </i>
        ‘to miss, yearn, pine for’,
        <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
         indāgāre
        </span>
        ‘to investigate, track’ &gt; Old Catalan
        <i>
         enagar
        </i>
        ‘to incite, induce’,
        <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
         odiāre
        </span>
        &gt; OCat
        <i>
         ujar
        </i>
        ‘to exhaust, fatigue’,
        <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
         pācificāre
        </span>
        &gt;
        <i>
         apaivagar
        </i>
        ‘to appease, mollify’,
        <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
         repudiāre
        </span>
        &gt;
        <i>
         rebutjar
        </i>
        ‘to reject, refuse’;
       </li>
       <li>
        nouns:
        <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
         brīsa
        </span>
        &gt;
        <i>
         brisa
        </i>
        ‘pomace’,
        <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
         buda
        </span>
        &gt;
        <i>
         boga
        </i>
        ‘reedmace’,
        <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
         catarrhu
        </span>
        &gt;
        <i>
         cadarn
        </i>
        ‘catarrh’,
        <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
         congesta
        </span>
        &gt;
        <i>
         congesta
        </i>
        ‘snowdrift’,
        <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
         dēlīrium
        </span>
        &gt;
        <i>
         deler
        </i>
        ‘ardor, passion’,
        <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
         fretu
        </span>
        &gt;
        <i>
         freu
        </i>
        ‘brake’,
        <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
         lābem
        </span>
        &gt;
        <i>
         (a)llau
        </i>
        ‘avalanche’,
        <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
         ōra
        </span>
        &gt;
        <i>
         vora
        </i>
        ‘edge, border’,
        <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
         pistrice
        </span>
        &gt;
        <i>
         pestriu
        </i>
        ‘fish species’,
        <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
         prūna
        </span>
        ‘live coal’ &gt;
        <i>
         espurna
        </i>
        ‘spark’,
        <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
         tardātiōnem
        </span>
        &gt;
        <i>
         tardaó
        </i>
        &gt;
        <i>
         tardor
        </i>
        ‘autumn’.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEBruguera20083046_44-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEBruguera20083046-44">
          [44]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Gothic_language" title="Gothic language">
        Gothic
       </a>
       superstrate produced different outcomes in Spanish and Catalan. For example, Catalan
       <i>
        <span lang="ca">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/fang#Catalan" title="wikt:fang">
          fang
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       "mud" and
       <i>
        <span lang="ca">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/rostir#Catalan" title="wikt:rostir">
          rostir
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       "to roast", of Germanic origin, contrast with Spanish
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/lodo#Spanish" title="wikt:lodo">
          lodo
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/asar#Spanish" title="wikt:asar">
          asar
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       , of Latin origin; whereas Catalan
       <i>
        <span lang="ca">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/filosa#Catalan" title="wikt:filosa">
          filosa
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       "spinning wheel" and
       <i>
        <span lang="ca">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/pols#Catalan" title="wikt:pols">
          pols
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       "temple", of Latin origin, contrast with Spanish
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/rueca#Spanish" title="wikt:rueca">
          rueca
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <span lang="es">
         <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/sien#Spanish" title="wikt:sien">
          sien
         </a>
        </span>
       </i>
       , of Germanic origin.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632_31-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The same happens with
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arabic_language" title="Arabic language">
        Arabic
       </a>
       loanwords. Thus, Catalan
       <i>
        alfàbia
       </i>
       "large earthenware jar" and
       <i>
        rajola
       </i>
       "tile", of Arabic origin, contrast with Spanish
       <i>
        tinaja
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        teja
       </i>
       , of Latin origin; whereas Catalan
       <i>
        oli
       </i>
       "oil" and
       <i>
        oliva
       </i>
       "olive", of Latin origin, contrast with Spanish
       <i>
        aceite
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        aceituna
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632_31-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, the Arabic element in Spanish is generally much more prevalent.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632_31-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Situated between two large linguistic blocks (Iberian Romance and Gallo-Romance), Catalan has many unique lexical choices, such as
       <i>
        enyorar
       </i>
       "to miss somebody",
       <i>
        apaivagar
       </i>
       "to calm somebody down", and
       <i>
        rebutjar
       </i>
       "reject".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632_31-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geographic_distribution">
        Geographic distribution
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Geographic distribution">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Catalan-speaking_territories">

       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">

        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_Countries" title="Catalan Countries">

       </a>
      </div>

      <p>
       Traditionally Catalan-speaking territories are sometimes called the
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pa%C3%AFsos_Catalans" title="Països Catalans">
         Països Catalans
        </a>
       </i>
       (Catalan Countries), a denomination based on cultural affinity and common heritage, that has also had a subsequent political interpretation but no official status. Various interpretations of the term may include some or all of these regions.
      </p>

         . The Andorrans speak a Western Catalan variety.

       <tr>
        <td>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Number_of_speakers">
        Number of speakers
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Number of speakers">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The number of people known to be fluent in Catalan varies depending on the sources used. A 2004 study did not count the total number of speakers, but estimated a total of 9–9.5 million by matching the percentage of speakers to the population of each area where Catalan is spoken.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The web site of the
       <a href="/wiki/Generalitat_de_Catalunya" title="Generalitat de Catalunya">
        Generalitat de Catalunya
       </a>
       estimated that as of 2004 there were 9,118,882 speakers of Catalan.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These figures only reflect potential speakers; today it is the native language of only 35.6% of the Catalan population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-habitual_47-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-habitual-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Ethnologue" title="Ethnologue">
         Ethnologue
        </a>
       </i>
       , Catalan had four million native speakers and five million second-language speakers in 2012.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-e18_38-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-e18-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The most important social characteristic of the Catalan language is that all the areas where it is spoken are bilingual in practice: together with the French language in Roussillon, with Italian in Alghero, with Spanish and French in Andorra and with Spanish in the rest of the territories.
      </p>
