      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Phonology">
        Phonology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Phonology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_phonology" title="Catalan phonology">
        Catalan phonology
       </a>
      </div>
      <table class="metadata mbox-small noprint selfref" role="presentation" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;width: 22em;">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
          <img alt="[]" data-file-height="100" data-file-width="75" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Parentesi_Quadre.svg/30px-Parentesi_Quadre.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Parentesi_Quadre.svg/45px-Parentesi_Quadre.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Parentesi_Quadre.svg/60px-Parentesi_Quadre.svg.png 2x" width="30"/>
         </a>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="vertical-align:middle; font-size:95%;">
         <b>
          This article contains
          <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
           IPA
          </a>
          phonetic symbols.
         </b>
         Without proper
         <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet#Fonts" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
          rendering support
         </a>
         , you may see
         <a href="/wiki/Specials_(Unicode_block)#Replacement_character" title="Specials (Unicode block)">
          question marks, boxes, or other symbols
         </a>
         instead of
         <a href="/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">
          Unicode
         </a>
         characters. For an introductory guide on IPA symbols, see
         <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">
          Help:IPA
         </a>
         .
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       Catalan phonology varies by dialect. Notable features include:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630_52-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Marked contrast of the vowel pairs /ɛ e/ and /ɔ o/, as in other
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_Romance" title="Western Romance">
         Western Romance
        </a>
        languages, other than
        <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
         Spanish
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630_52-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630-52">
          [52]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Lack of
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diphthongization" title="Diphthongization">
         diphthongization
        </a>
        of
        <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">
         Latin
        </a>
        short
        <i>
         ĕ
        </i>
        ,
        <i>
         ŏ
        </i>
        , as in
        <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">
         Galician
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">
         Portuguese
        </a>
        , but unlike French, Spanish, or Italian.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630_52-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630-52">
          [52]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Abundance of diphthongs containing /w/, as in Galician and Portuguese.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630_52-3">
         <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630-52">
          [52]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       In contrast to other Romance languages, Catalan has many
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monosyllabic" title="Monosyllabic">
        monosyllabic
       </a>
       words, and these may end in a wide variety of consonants, including some
       <a href="/wiki/Consonant_cluster" title="Consonant cluster">
        consonant clusters
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630_52-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Additionally, Catalan has
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Final_obstruent_devoicing" title="Final obstruent devoicing">
        final obstruent devoicing
       </a>
       , which gives rise to an abundance of such couplets as
       <i>
        amic
       </i>
       "(male friend") vs.
       <i>
        amiga
       </i>
       ("female friend").
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630_52-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Catalan" title="Central Catalan">
        Central Catalan
       </a>
       pronunciation is considered to be standard for the language.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20105_53-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20105-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The descriptions below are mostly representative of this variety.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       For the differences in pronunciation between the different dialects, see the section on
       <a href="#Dialect_pronunciation_section">
        pronunciation of dialects
       </a>
       in this article.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Vowels">
        Vowels
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Vowels">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Catalan_vowel_chart.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="720" data-file-width="980" height="184" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Catalan_vowel_chart.svg/250px-Catalan_vowel_chart.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Catalan_vowel_chart.svg/375px-Catalan_vowel_chart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Catalan_vowel_chart.svg/500px-Catalan_vowel_chart.svg.png 2x" width="250"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Catalan_vowel_chart.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Vowel" title="Vowel">
          Vowels
         </a>
         of Standard Eastern Catalan
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarbonellLlisterri199962_55-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarbonellLlisterri199962-55">
           [55]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Catalan has inherited the typical vowel system of
       <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">
        Vulgar Latin
       </a>
       , with seven stressed phonemes:
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /a ɛ e i ɔ o u/
       </span>
       , a common feature in
       <a href="/wiki/Western_Romance_languages" title="Western Romance languages">
        Western Romance
       </a>
       , except
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630_52-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Balearic_dialect" title="Balearic dialect">
        Balearic
       </a>
       also has instances of stressed /ə/.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler200537,53–54_56-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler200537,53–54-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Dialects differ in the different degrees of
       <a href="/wiki/Vowel_reduction" title="Vowel reduction">
        vowel reduction
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler200537_57-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler200537-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the incidence of the pair /ɛ e/.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler200538_58-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler200538-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Catalan" title="Central Catalan">
        Central Catalan
       </a>
       , unstressed vowels reduce to three:
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /a e ɛ/ &gt; [ə]
       </span>
       ;
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /o ɔ u/ &gt; [u]
       </span>
       ;
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /i/
       </span>
       remains distinct.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler200554_59-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler200554-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The other dialects have different vowel reduction processes (see the section
       <a href="#Dialect_pronunciation_section">
        pronunciation of dialects
       </a>
       in this article).
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable" style="margin:auto; text-align:center;">

      <div style="clear:both;">
      </div>
      <p>
       The consonant system of Catalan is rather conservative, shared with most modern
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_Romance" title="Western Romance">
        Western Romance
       </a>
       languages.
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /l/
        </span>
        has a
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dark_l" title="Dark l">
         velarized
        </a>
        allophone in
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Syllable_coda" title="Syllable coda">
         syllable coda
        </a>
        position in most dialects.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERecasensEspinosa200520_62-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERecasensEspinosa200520-62">
          [62]
         </a>
        </sup>
        However,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /l/
        </span>
        is velarized irrespective of position in Eastern dialects like Majorcan
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERecasensEspinosa20053_63-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERecasensEspinosa20053-63">
          [63]
         </a>
        </sup>
        and standard Eastern Catalan.
       </li>
       <li>
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /v/
        </span>
        occurs in Balearic,
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECarbonellLlisterri199253_64-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECarbonellLlisterri199253-64">
          [64]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alguerese" title="Alguerese">
         Alguerese
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Valencian#Consonants" title="Valencian">
         standard Valencian
        </a>
        and some areas in southern Catalonia.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEVeny200751_65-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEVeny200751-65">
          [65]
         </a>
        </sup>
        It has
        <a href="/wiki/Betacism" title="Betacism">
         merged
        </a>
        with
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /b/
        </span>
        elsewhere.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
         <a href="#cite_note-66">
          [66]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Voiced obstruents undergo
        <a href="/wiki/Final-obstruent_devoicing" title="Final-obstruent devoicing">
         final-obstruent devoicing
        </a>
        :
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /b/ &gt; [p], /d/ &gt; [t], /ɡ/ &gt; [k]
        </span>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELloret2003278_67-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELloret2003278-67">
          [67]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Voiced stops become
        <a href="/wiki/Lenition" title="Lenition">
         lenited
        </a>
        to approximants in syllable onsets, after continuants:
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /b/ &gt;
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [
          <a href="/wiki/Voiced_bilabial_fricative" title="Voiced bilabial fricative">
           β
          </a>
          ]
         </span>
         , /d/ &gt;
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [
          <a href="/wiki/Voiced_dental_fricative" title="Voiced dental fricative">
           ð
          </a>
          ]
         </span>
         , /ɡ/ &gt;
         <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
          [
          <a href="/wiki/Voiced_velar_fricative" title="Voiced velar fricative">
           ɣ
          </a>
          ]
         </span>
        </span>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_68-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-68">
          [68]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Exceptions include
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /d/
        </span>
        after
        <a href="/wiki/Lateral_consonant" title="Lateral consonant">
         lateral consonants
        </a>
        , and
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /b/
        </span>
        after
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /f/
        </span>
        . In coda position, these sounds are realized as stops,
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69">
         <a href="#cite_note-69">
          [69]
         </a>
        </sup>
        except in some Valencian dialects where they are lenited.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERecasensEspinosa20051_70-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERecasensEspinosa20051-70">
          [70]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        There is some confusion in the literature about the precise phonetic characteristics of
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ʃ/
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ʒ/
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /tʃ/
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /dʒ/
        </span>
        . Some sources
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carbonell_1992_53_71-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-Carbonell_1992_53-71">
          [71]
         </a>
        </sup>
        describe them as "postalveolar". Others
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
         <a href="#cite_note-72">
          [72]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
         <a href="#cite_note-73">
          [73]
         </a>
        </sup>
        as "back alveolo-palatal", implying that the characters ⟨
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         ɕ ʑ tɕ dʑ
        </span>
        ⟩ would be more accurate. However, in all literature only the characters for
        <a href="/wiki/Palato-alveolar_consonant" title="Palato-alveolar consonant">
         palato-alveolar
        </a>
        affricates and fricatives are used, even when the same sources use ⟨
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         ɕ ʑ
        </span>
        ⟩ for other languages like Polish and Chinese.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
         <a href="#cite_note-74">
          [74]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
         <a href="#cite_note-75">
          [75]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERecasensEspinosa2007145_76-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERecasensEspinosa2007145-76">
          [76]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        The distribution of the two rhotics
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /r/
        </span>
        and
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ɾ/
        </span>
        closely parallels
        <a href="/wiki/Spanish_phonology#Alternations" title="Spanish phonology">
         that of Spanish
        </a>
        . Between vowels, the two contrast, but they are otherwise in complementary distribution: in the onset of the first syllable in a word,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_trill" title="Alveolar trill">
          r
         </a>
         ]
        </span>
        appears unless preceded by a consonant. Dialects vary in regards to rhotics in the coda with Western Catalan generally featuring
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_flap" title="Alveolar flap">
          ɾ
         </a>
         ]
        </span>
        and Central Catalan dialects featuring a weakly trilled
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_trill" title="Alveolar trill">
          r
         </a>
         ]
        </span>
        unless it precedes a vowel-initial word in the same
        <a href="/wiki/Prosodic_unit" title="Prosodic unit">
         prosodic unit
        </a>
        , in which case
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_flap" title="Alveolar flap">
          ɾ
         </a>
         ]
        </span>
        appears.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPadgett20032_77-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPadgett20032-77">
          [77]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        In careful speech,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /n/
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /m/
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /l/
        </span>
        may be
        <a href="/wiki/Gemination" title="Gemination">
         geminated
        </a>
        . Geminated
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         /ʎ/
        </span>
        may also occur.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Carbonell_1992_53_71-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-Carbonell_1992_53-71">
          [71]
         </a>
        </sup>
        Some analyze intervocalic
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         [r]
        </span>
        as the result of gemination of a single rhotic phoneme.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
         <a href="#cite_note-78">
          [78]
         </a>
        </sup>
        This is similar to the common analysis of Spanish and
        <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">
         Portuguese
        </a>
        rhotics.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
         <a href="#cite_note-79">
          [79]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Phonological_evolution">
        Phonological evolution
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Phonological evolution">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Phonological_history_of_Catalan" title="Phonological history of Catalan">
        Phonological history of Catalan
       </a>
      </div>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sociolinguistics">
        Sociolinguistics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Sociolinguistics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Catalan
       <a href="/wiki/Sociolinguistics" title="Sociolinguistics">
        sociolinguistics
       </a>
       studies the situation of Catalan in the world and the different varieties that this language presents. It is a subdiscipline of Catalan
       <a href="/wiki/Philology" title="Philology">
        philology
       </a>
       and other affine studies and has as an objective to analyse the relation between the Catalan language, the speakers and the close reality (including the one of other languages in contact).
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Preferential_subjects_of_study">
        Preferential subjects of study
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Preferential subjects of study">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Dialect" title="Dialect">
         Dialects
        </a>
        of Catalan
       </li>
       <li>
        Variations of Catalan by class, gender, profession, age and level of studies
       </li>
       <li>
        Process of
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Linguistic_normalisation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Linguistic normalisation (page does not exist)">
         linguistic normalisation
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Relations between Catalan and
        <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
         Spanish
        </a>
        or
        <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">
         French
        </a>
       </li>
       <li>
        Perception on the language of Catalan speakers and non-speakers
       </li>
       <li>
        Presence of Catalan in several fields: tagging, public function, media, professional sectors
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Dialects">
        Dialects
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Dialects">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_dialects" title="Catalan dialects">
        Catalan dialects
       </a>
      </div>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">
        Overview
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Overview">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Catalandialects.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="934" data-file-width="772" height="363" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Catalandialects.png/300px-Catalandialects.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Catalandialects.png/450px-Catalandialects.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/Catalandialects.png/600px-Catalandialects.png 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Catalandialects.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Main dialects of Catalan
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20106_80-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20106-80">
           [80]
          </a>
         </sup>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler20052_81-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler20052-81">
           [81]
          </a>
         </sup>
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECosta_Carreras20094_82-0">
          <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECosta_Carreras20094-82">
           [82]
          </a>
         </sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The dialects of the Catalan language feature a relative uniformity, especially when compared to other Romance languages;
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoll195847_37-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoll195847-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       both in terms of
       <a href="/wiki/Vocabulary" title="Vocabulary">
        vocabulary
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Semantics" title="Semantics">
        semantics
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Syntax" title="Syntax">
        syntax
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Morphology_(linguistics)" title="Morphology (linguistics)">
        morphology
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Phonology" title="Phonology">
        phonology
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana634–635_83-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana634–635-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Mutual intelligibility between dialects is very high,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler20051_23-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler20051-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates20095_84-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECosta_CarrerasYates20095-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20105_53-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20105-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       estimates ranging from 90% to 95%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ethnologue_85-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ethnologue-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The only exception is the isolated idiosyncratic
       <a href="/wiki/Algherese_dialect" title="Algherese dialect">
        Alguerese dialect
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoll195847_37-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoll195847-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Catalan is split in two major dialectal blocks: Eastern Catalan, and Western Catalan.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20105_53-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20105-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana634–635_83-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana634–635-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The main difference lies in the treatment of unstressed
       <i>
        a
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        e
       </i>
       ; which have merged to /ə/ in Eastern dialects, but which remain distinct as /a/ and /e/ in Western dialects.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoll195847_37-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMoll195847-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20105_53-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20105-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are a few other differences in pronunciation, verbal morphology, and vocabulary.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler20051_23-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler20051-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Western Catalan comprises the two dialects of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northwestern_Catalan" title="Northwestern Catalan">
        Northwestern Catalan
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Valencian" title="Valencian">
        Valencian
       </a>
       ; the Eastern block comprises four dialects:
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Catalan" title="Central Catalan">
        Central Catalan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Balearic_dialect" title="Balearic dialect">
        Balearic
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Northern_Catalan" title="Northern Catalan">
        Rossellonese
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Algherese_dialect" title="Algherese dialect">
        Alguerese
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20105_53-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20105-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Each dialect can be further subdivided in several subdialects. The terms "Catalan" and "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Valencian_language" title="Valencian language">
        Valencian
       </a>
       " (respectively used in
       <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">
        Catalonia
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Valencian_Community" title="Valencian Community">
        Valencian Community
       </a>
       ) are two varieties of the same language.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-avl.gva.es_86-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-avl.gva.es-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are two institutions regulating the two standard varieties, the
       <a href="/wiki/Institut_d%27Estudis_Catalans" title="Institut d'Estudis Catalans">
        Institute of Catalan Studies
       </a>
       in Catalonia and the
       <a href="/wiki/Acad%C3%A8mia_Valenciana_de_la_Llengua" title="Acadèmia Valenciana de la Llengua">
        Valencian Academy of the Language
       </a>
       in the Valencian Community.
      </p>
      <p>
       Central Catalan is considered the standard pronunciation of the language and has the highest number of speakers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20105_53-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20105-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is spoken in the densely populated regions of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barcelona_Province_(Spain)" title="Barcelona Province (Spain)">
        Barcelona province
       </a>
       , the eastern half of the province of Tarragona, and most of the province of Girona.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20105_53-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20105-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Catalan has an inflectional grammar. Nouns have two
       <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_gender" title="Grammatical gender">
        genders
       </a>
       (masculine, feminine), and two
       <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_number" title="Grammatical number">
        numbers
       </a>
       (singular, plural). Pronouns additionally can have a neuter gender, and some are also inflected for
       <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_case" title="Grammatical case">
        case
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/T%E2%80%93V_distinction" title="T–V distinction">
        politeness
       </a>
       , and can be combined in very complex ways. Verbs are split in several paradigms and are inflected for
       <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_person" title="Grammatical person">
        person
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_number" title="Grammatical number">
        number
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_tense" title="Grammatical tense">
        tense
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_aspect" title="Grammatical aspect">
        aspect
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_mood" title="Grammatical mood">
        mood
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_gender" title="Grammatical gender">
        gender
       </a>
       . In terms of pronunciation, Catalan has many words ending in a wide variety of consonants and some consonant clusters, in contrast with many other Romance languages.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630_52-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center;">

        </sup>

         <a href="/wiki/Alghero" title="Alghero">

         </a>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Pronunciation">
        <span id="Dialect_pronunciation_section">
        </span>
        Pronunciation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Pronunciation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Vowels_2">
        Vowels
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Vowels">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Catalan has inherited the typical vowel system of
       <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">
        Vulgar Latin
       </a>
       , with seven stressed phonemes:
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /a ɛ e i ɔ o u/
       </span>
       , a common feature in
       <a href="/wiki/Western_Romance_languages" title="Western Romance languages">
        Western Romance
       </a>
       , except
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630_52-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Balearic_dialect" title="Balearic dialect">
        Balearic
       </a>
       has also instances of stressed /ə/.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler200537,53–54_56-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler200537,53–54-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Dialects differ in the different degrees of
       <a href="/wiki/Vowel_reduction" title="Vowel reduction">
        vowel reduction
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler200537_57-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler200537-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the incidence of the pair /ɛ e/.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler200538_58-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler200538-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Catalan" title="Eastern Catalan">
        Eastern Catalan
       </a>
       (except Majorcan), unstressed vowels reduce to three:
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /a e ɛ/ &gt; [ə]
       </span>
       ;
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /o ɔ u/ &gt; [u]
       </span>
       ;
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /i/
       </span>
       remains distinct.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler200554_59-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler200554-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are a few instances of unreduced [e], [o] in some words.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler200554_59-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler200554-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alguerese" title="Alguerese">
        Alguerese
       </a>
       has lowered [ə] to [a].
      </p>
      <p>
       In Majorcan, unstressed vowels reduce to four:
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /a e ɛ/
       </span>
       follow the Eastern Catalan reduction pattern; however
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /o ɔ/
       </span>
       reduce to
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [o]
       </span>
       , with
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /u/
       </span>
       remaining distinct, as in Western Catalan.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler200553–54_88-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler200553–54-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_Catalan" title="Western Catalan">
        Western Catalan
       </a>
       , unstressed vowels reduce to five:
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /e ɛ/ &gt; [e]
       </span>
       ;
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /o ɔ/ &gt; [o]
       </span>
       ;
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /a u i/
       </span>
       remain distinct.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler200553_89-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler200553-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
        <a href="#cite_note-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This reduction pattern, inherited from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proto-Romance" title="Proto-Romance">
        Proto-Romance
       </a>
       , is also found in
       <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">
        Italian
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler200553_89-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler200553-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Some Western dialects present further reduction or vowel harmony in some cases.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler200553_89-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler200553-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTERecasens199675–76,128–129_91-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTERecasens199675–76,128–129-91">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Central, Western, and Balearic differ in the lexical incidence of stressed /e/ and /ɛ/.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler200538_58-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler200538-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Usually, words with /ɛ/ in Central Catalan correspond to /ə/ in Balearic and /e/ in Western Catalan.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler200538_58-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler200538-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Words with /e/ in Balearic almost always have /e/ in Central and Western Catalan as well.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Vagueness" title="Wikipedia:Vagueness">
          <span title="This information is too vague. (April 2014)">
           vague
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler200538_58-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler200538-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As a result, Central Catalan has a much higher incidence of /ɛ/.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler200538_58-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler200538-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table>
       <tr>

      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Consonants_2">
        Consonants
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Consonants">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg">
          <img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/>
         </a>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          <b>
           This section needs expansion
          </b>
          .
          <small>
           You can help by
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">
            adding to it
           </a>
           .
          </small>
          <small>
           <i>
            (March 2014)
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Morphology">
        Morphology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Morphology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Western Catalan: In verbs, the ending for 1st-person present indicative is -
       <i>
        e
       </i>
       in verbs of the 1st conjugation and -∅ in verbs of the 2nd and 3rd conjugations in most of the Valencian Community, or -
       <i>
        o
       </i>
       in all verb conjugations in the Northern Valencian Community and Western Catalonia.
       <br/>
       E.g.
       <i>
        parle
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        tem
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        sent
       </i>
       (Valencian);
       <i>
        parlo
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        temo
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        sento
       </i>
       (Northwestern Catalan).
      </p>
      <p>
       Eastern Catalan: In verbs, the ending for 1st-person present indicative is -
       <i>
        o
       </i>
       , -
       <i>
        i
       </i>
       , or -∅ in all conjugations.
       <br/>
       E.g.
       <i>
        parlo
       </i>
       (Central),
       <i>
        parl
       </i>
       (Balearic), and
       <i>
        parli
       </i>
       (Northern), all meaning ('I speak').
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable" style="text-align: center;">
       <caption>
        1st-person singular present indicative forms
       </caption>
       <tr>
        <th colspan="3," rowspan="2">
         Conjugation
        </th>
        <th colspan="3">
         Eastern Catalan
        </th>
        <th colspan="2">
         Western Catalan
        </th>
        <th rowspan="2">
         Gloss
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th>

        </th>
        <th>

        </th>
        <th>
         Balearic
        </th>
        <th>
         Valencian
        </th>
        <th>
         Northwestern
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th colspan="3">
         1st
        </th>
        <td>
         <i>
          parlo
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          parli
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          parl
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          parle
         </i>
         or
         <i>
          parlo
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          parlo
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         'I speak'
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th colspan="3">
         2nd
        </th>
        <td>
         <i>
          temo
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          temi
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          tem
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          tem
         </i>
         or
         <i>
          temo
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          temo
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         'I fear'
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2," rowspan="2">
         3rd
        </th>
        <th>
         <small>
          pure
         </small>
        </th>
        <td>
         <i>
          sento
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          senti
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          sent
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          sent
         </i>
         or
         <i>
          sento
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          sento
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         'I feel', 'I hear'
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th>
         <small>
          inchoative
         </small>
        </th>
        <td>
         <i>
          poleixo
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          poleixi
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          poleix
         </i>
         or
         <i>
          polesc
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          polisc
         </i>
         or
         <i>
          pol(e)ixo
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          pol(e)ixo
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         'I polish'
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       Western Catalan: In verbs, the inchoative endings are -
       <i>
        isc
       </i>
       /-
       <i>
        ixo
       </i>
       , -
       <i>
        ix
       </i>
       , -
       <i>
        ixen
       </i>
       , -
       <i>
        isca
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Eastern Catalan: In verbs, the inchoative endings are -
       <i>
        eixo
       </i>
       , -
       <i>
        eix
       </i>
       , -
       <i>
        eixen
       </i>
       , -
       <i>
        eixi
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Western Catalan: In nouns and adjectives, maintenance of
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /n/
       </span>
       of medieval plurals in
       <a href="/wiki/Proparoxytone" title="Proparoxytone">
        proparoxytone
       </a>
       words.
       <br/>
       E.g.
       <i>
        hòmens
       </i>
       'men',
       <i>
        jóvens
       </i>
       'youth'.
      </p>
      <p>
       Eastern Catalan: In nouns and adjectives, loss of
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /n/
       </span>
       of medieval plurals in proparoxytone words.
       <br/>
       E.g.
       <i>
        homes
       </i>
       'men',
       <i>
        joves
       </i>
       'youth'.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Vocabulary">
        Vocabulary
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Vocabulary">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Despite its relative lexical unity, the two dialectal blocks of Catalan (Eastern and Western) show some differences in word choices.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632_31-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Any lexical divergence within any of the two groups can be explained as an archaism. Also, usually
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Catalan" title="Central Catalan">
        Central Catalan
       </a>
       acts as an innovative element.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632_31-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable">

        Selection of different words between Western and Eastern Catalan
       </caption>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Standards">
        Standards
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Standards">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Institut_d%27Estudis_Catalans" title="Institut d'Estudis Catalans">
        Institut d'Estudis Catalans
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Acad%C3%A8mia_Valenciana_de_la_Llengua" title="Acadèmia Valenciana de la Llengua">
        Acadèmia Valenciana de la Llengua
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Casa_de_Convalesc%C3%A8ncia_-_IEC.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1899" data-file-width="2857" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Casa_de_Convalesc%C3%A8ncia_-_IEC.JPG/300px-Casa_de_Convalesc%C3%A8ncia_-_IEC.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Casa_de_Convalesc%C3%A8ncia_-_IEC.JPG/450px-Casa_de_Convalesc%C3%A8ncia_-_IEC.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Casa_de_Convalesc%C3%A8ncia_-_IEC.JPG/600px-Casa_de_Convalesc%C3%A8ncia_-_IEC.JPG 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Casa_de_Convalesc%C3%A8ncia_-_IEC.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Casa de Convalescència, Headquarters of the Institut d'Estudis Catalans
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <table class="wikitable" style="width:250px; float:right; margin-left: 1em;">
       <caption>
        Written varieties
       </caption>
       <tr>

        </th>

        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>

         </i>
        </td>

        </td>
       </tr>

        </td>
       </tr>

         </i>

        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>

        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>

        </td>
       </tr>

       </tr>
       <tr>

        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>

       </tr>

        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>

         </i>

         </i>

         men
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <i>
          servei
         </i>
