        <td>
         <i>
          servici
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         service
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       Standard Catalan, virtually accepted by all speakers,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler2003207_25-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler2003207-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       is mostly based on Eastern Catalan,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20105_53-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20105-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler2003170_93-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler2003170-93">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which is the most widely used dialect. Nevertheless, the standards of the Valencian Community and the Balearics admit alternative forms, mostly traditional ones, which are not current in eastern Catalonia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler2003170_93-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler2003170-93">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The most notable difference between both standards is some tonic ⟨e⟩ accentuation, for instance:
       <i>
        francès, anglès
       </i>
       (IEC) –
       <i>
        francés, anglés
       </i>
       (AVL). Nevertheless, AVL's standard keeps the grave accent ⟨è⟩, without pronouncing this ⟨e⟩ as
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /ɛ/
       </span>
       , in some words like:
       <i>
        què
       </i>
       ('what'), or
       <i>
        València
       </i>
       . Other divergences include the use of ⟨tl⟩ (AVL) in some words instead of ⟨tll⟩ like in
       <i>
        ametla
       </i>
       /
       <i>
        ametlla
       </i>
       ('almond'),
       <i>
        espatla
       </i>
       /
       <i>
        espatlla
       </i>
       ('back'), the use of elided demonstratives (
       <i>
        este
       </i>
       'this',
       <i>
        eixe
       </i>
       'that') in the same level as reinforced ones (
       <i>
        aquest, aqueix
       </i>
       ) or the use of many verbal forms common in Valencian, and some of these common in the rest of Western Catalan too, like subjunctive mood or inchoative conjugation in -
       <i>
        ix
       </i>
       - at the same level as -
       <i>
        eix
       </i>
       - or the priority use of -
       <i>
        e
       </i>
       morpheme in 1st person singular in present indicative (-
       <i>
        ar
       </i>
       verbs):
       <i>
        jo compre
       </i>
       instead of
       <i>
        jo compro
       </i>
       ('I buy').
      </p>
      <p>
       In the Balearic Islands, IEC's standard is used but adapted for the Balearic dialect by the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_Balearic_Islands" title="University of the Balearic Islands">
        University of the Balearic Islands
       </a>
       's philological section. In this way, for instance, IEC says it is correct writing
       <i>
        cantam
       </i>
       as much as
       <i>
        cantem
       </i>
       ('we sing') but the University says that the priority form in the Balearic Islands must be "
       <i>
        cantam
       </i>
       " in all fields. Another feature of the Balearic standard is the non-ending in the 1st person singular present indicative:
       <i>
        jo compr
       </i>
       ('I buy'),
       <i>
        jo tem
       </i>
       ('I fear'),
       <i>
        jo dorm
       </i>
       ('I sleep').
      </p>
      <p>
       In Alghero, the IEC has adapted its standard to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alguerese" title="Alguerese">
        Alguerese dialect
       </a>
       . In this standard one can find, among other features: the definite article
       <i>
        lo
       </i>
       instead of
       <i>
        el
       </i>
       , special possessive pronouns and determinants
       <i>
        la mia
       </i>
       ('mine'),
       <i>
        lo sou/la sua
       </i>
       ('his/her'),
       <i>
        lo tou/la tua
       </i>
       ('yours'), and so on, the use of
       <i>
        -v-
       </i>
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        /v/
       </span>
       in the imperfect tense in all conjugations:
       <i>
        cantava
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        creixiva
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        llegiva
       </i>
       ; the use of many archaic words, usual words in Alguerese:
       <i>
        manco
       </i>
       instead of
       <i>
        menys
       </i>
       ('less'),
       <i>
        calqui u
       </i>
       instead of
       <i>
        algú
       </i>
       ('someone'),
       <i>
        qual/quala
       </i>
       instead of
       <i>
        quin/quina
       </i>
       ('which'), and so on; and the adaptation of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weak_pronouns_in_Catalan" title="Weak pronouns in Catalan">
        weak pronouns
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2011, the
       <a href="/wiki/Aragon" title="Aragon">
        Aragonese government
       </a>
       passed a decree for the establishment of a new language regulator of Catalan in
       <a href="/wiki/La_Franja" title="La Franja">
        La Franja
       </a>
       (the so-called Catalan-speaking areas of Aragon). The new entity, designated as
       <i>
        <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Acad%C3%A8mia_Aragonesa_del_Catal%C3%A0&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Acadèmia Aragonesa del Català (page does not exist)">
         Acadèmia Aragonesa del Català
        </a>
       </i>
       , shall allow a facultative education in Catalan and a standardization of the Catalan language in
       <a href="/wiki/La_Franja" title="La Franja">
        La Franja
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Status_of_Valencian">
        <span id="About_Valencian">
        </span>
        Status of Valencian
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Status of Valencian">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" role="presentation" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <img alt="" class="noviewer" data-file-height="430" data-file-width="410" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/38px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/57px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4c/Wikisource-logo.svg/76px-Wikisource-logo.svg.png 2x" width="38"/>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text plainlist">
         Catalan
         <a href="/wiki/Wikisource" title="Wikisource">
          Wikisource
         </a>
         has original text related to this article:
         <div style="margin-left: 10px;">
          <b>
           <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/ca:Dictamen_sobre_els_principis_i_criteris_per_a_la_defensa_de_la_denominaci%C3%B3_i_l%27entitat_del_valenci%C3%A0" title="s:ca:Dictamen sobre els principis i criteris per a la defensa de la denominació i l'entitat del valencià">
            AVL: Dictamen sobre els principis i criteris per a la defensa de la denominació i l'entitat del valencià
           </a>
          </b>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Valencian" title="Valencian">
        Valencian
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Valencian_language_controversy" title="Valencian language controversy">
        Valencian language controversy
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Blaverism" title="Blaverism">
        Blaverism
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Anti-Catalanism" title="Anti-Catalanism">
        Anti-Catalanism
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Subdialectes_del_valenci%C3%A0.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1090" data-file-width="643" height="373" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Subdialectes_del_valenci%C3%A0.svg/220px-Subdialectes_del_valenci%C3%A0.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Subdialectes_del_valenci%C3%A0.svg/330px-Subdialectes_del_valenci%C3%A0.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Subdialectes_del_valenci%C3%A0.svg/440px-Subdialectes_del_valenci%C3%A0.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Subdialectes_del_valenci%C3%A0.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Subdialects of Valencian
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Valencian is classified as a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_Catalan" title="Western Catalan">
        Western
       </a>
       dialect, along with the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northwestern_Catalan" title="Northwestern Catalan">
        northwestern
       </a>
       varieties spoken in Western Catalonia (provinces of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lleida_province" title="Lleida province">
        Lleida
       </a>
       and the western half of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tarragona_province" title="Tarragona province">
        Tarragona
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20105_53-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEFeldhausen20105-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler20052–3_87-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler20052–3-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The various forms of Catalan and Valencian are mutually intelligible (ranging from 90% to 95%)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ethnologue_85-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ethnologue-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Linguists, including Valencian scholars, deal with Catalan and Valencian as the same language. The official regulating body of the language of the Valencian Community, the
       <a href="/wiki/Acad%C3%A8mia_Valenciana_de_la_Llengua" title="Acadèmia Valenciana de la Llengua">
        Valencian Academy of Language
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        Acadèmia Valenciana de la Llengua,
       </i>
       AVL) declares the linguistic unity between Valencian and Catalan varieties.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dictalmen_AVL_12-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-dictalmen_AVL-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="quotebox pullquote" style="float: left; clear: left; margin: 0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0; width:72%; padding: 10px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
       <div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
        <div>
         [T]he historical patrimonial language of the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Valencian_people" title="Valencian people">
          Valencian people
         </a>
         , from a philological standpoint, is the same shared by the autonomous communities of
         <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">
          Catalonia
         </a>
         and
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Balearic_islands" title="Balearic islands">
          Balearic islands
         </a>
         , and
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Principality_of_Andorra" title="Principality of Andorra">
          Principality of Andorra
         </a>
         . Additionally, it is the patrimonial historical language of other territories of the ancient
         <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Aragon" title="Crown of Aragon">
          Crown of Aragon
         </a>
         [...] The different varieties of these territories constitute a language, that is, a "linguistic system" [...] From this group of varieties, Valencian has the same hierarchy and dignity as any other dialectal modality of that linguistic system [...]
        </div>
       </div>
       <cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">
        Ruling of the Valencian Language Academy of 9 February 2005, extract of point 1.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAcadèmia_Valenciana_de_la_Llengua2005_94-0">
         <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEAcadèmia_Valenciana_de_la_Llengua2005-94">
          [94]
         </a>
        </sup>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
         <a href="#cite_note-95">
          [95]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </cite>
      </div>
      <p>
       The AVL, created by the Valencian parliament, is in charge of dictating the official rules governing the use of Valencian, and its standard is based on the Norms of Castelló (
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Normes_de_Castell%C3%B3" title="Normes de Castelló">
         Normes de Castelló
        </a>
       </i>
       ). Currently, everyone who writes in Valencian uses this standard, except the Royal Academy of Valencian Culture (
       <i>
        Acadèmia de Cultura Valenciana
       </i>
       , RACV), which uses for Valencian an independent standard.
      </p>
      <p>
       Despite the position of the official organizations, an opinion poll carried out between 2001 and 2004
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
       showed that the majority of the Valencian people consider Valencian different from Catalan. This position is promoted by people who do not use Valencian regularly.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler2003207_25-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler2003207-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Furthermore, the data indicates that younger generations educated in Valencian are much less likely to hold these views. A minority of Valencian scholars active in fields other than linguistics defends the position of the Royal Academy of Valencian Culture (
       <i>
        Acadèmia de Cultura Valenciana
       </i>
       , RACV), which uses for Valencian a standard independent from Catalan.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
        <a href="#cite_note-97">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       This clash of opinions has sparked much controversy. For example, during the drafting of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Constitution" title="European Constitution">
        European Constitution
       </a>
       in 2004, the Spanish government supplied the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
        EU
       </a>
       with translations of the text into
       <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">
        Basque
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">
        Galician
       </a>
       , Catalan, and Valencian, but the latter two were identical.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
        <a href="#cite_note-98">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Vocabulary_2">
        Vocabulary
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Vocabulary">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Word_choices">
        Word choices
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Word choices">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Despite its relative lexical unity, the two dialectal blocks of Catalan (Eastern and Western) show some differences in word choices.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632_31-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Any lexical divergence within any of the two groups can be explained as an archaism. Also, usually
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Catalan" title="Central Catalan">
        Central Catalan
       </a>
       acts as an innovative element.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632_31-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Literary Catalan allows the use of words from different dialects, except those of very restricted use.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632_31-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, from the 19th century onwards, there has been a tendency towards favoring words of Northern dialects to the detriment of others,
       <span class="clarify-content" style="padding-left:0.1em; padding-right:0.1em; color:#595959; border:1px solid #DDD;">
        even though nowadays there is a greater freedom of choice.
       </span>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Clarify" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">
          <span title="This passage needs to be better explained. (July 2016)">
           clarify
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632_31-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Latin_and_Greek_loanwords">
        Latin and Greek loanwords
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Latin and Greek loanwords">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Like other languages, Catalan has a large list of loanwords from Greek and Latin. This process started very early, and one can find such examples in
       <a href="/wiki/Ramon_Llull" title="Ramon Llull">
        Ramon Llull
       </a>
       's work.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632_31-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the 14th and 15th centuries Catalan had a far greater number of Greco-Latin loanwords than other Romance languages, as is attested for example in
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ro%C3%ADs_de_Corella&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Roís de Corella (page does not exist)">
        Roís de Corella
       </a>
       's writings.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632_31-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana632-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The incorporation of learned, or "bookish" words from its own ancestor language,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_language" title="Latin language">
        Latin
       </a>
       , into Catalan is arguably another form of lexical borrowing through the influence of
       <a href="/wiki/Classical_Latin" title="Classical Latin">
        written language
       </a>
       and the liturgical language of the Church. Throughout the Middle Ages and into the early modern period, most literate Catalan speakers were also literate in Latin; and thus they easily adopted Latin words into their writing—and eventually speech—in Catalan.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Word_formation">
        Word formation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Word formation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The process of
       <a href="/wiki/Morphological_derivation" title="Morphological derivation">
        morphological derivation
       </a>
       in Catalan follows the same principles as the other
       <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">
        Romance languages
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631_99-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       where
       <a href="/wiki/Agglutination" title="Agglutination">
        agglutination
       </a>
       is common. Many times, several affixes are appended to a preexisting lexeme, and some sound alternations can occur, for example
       <i>
        elèctri
        <b>
         c
        </b>
       </i>
       [əˈlɛktri
       <b>
        k
       </b>
       ] ("electrical") vs.
       <i>
        electri
        <b>
         c
        </b>
        itat
       </i>
       [ələktri
       <b>
        s
       </b>
       iˈtat].
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prefixes" title="Prefixes">
        Prefixes
       </a>
       are usually appended to verbs, as in
       <i>
        <b>
         pre
        </b>
        veure
       </i>
       ("foresee").
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631_99-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       There is greater regularity in the process of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Word-compounding" title="Word-compounding">
        word-compounding
       </a>
       , where one can find compounded words formed much like those in English.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631_99-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <table class="wikitable">
       <caption>
        Common types of word compounds in Catalan
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631_99-3">
         <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631-99">
          [99]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </caption>
       <tr>
        <th>
         Type
        </th>
        <th>
         Example
        </th>
        <th>
         Gloss
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         two nouns, the second assimilated to the first
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          paper moneda
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         "banknote paper"
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         noun delimited by an adjective
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          estat major
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         "military staff"
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         noun delimited by another noun and a preposition
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          màquina d'escriure
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         "typewriter"
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         verb radical with a nominal object
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          <b>
           para
          </b>
          caigudes
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         "parachute"
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         noun delimited by an adjective, with adjectival value
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          pit-roig
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         "robin" (bird)
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Writing_system">
        Writing system
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Writing system">

        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>

      <p>
       Catalan uses the
       <a href="/wiki/Latin_script" title="Latin script">
        Latin script
       </a>
       , with some added symbols and digraphs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler20056_100-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler20056-100">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_orthography" title="Catalan orthography">
        Catalan orthography
       </a>
       is systematic and largely phonologically based.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler20056_100-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler20056-100">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>

         in other contexts
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          feliç
         </i>
         ("happy-
         <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
          masculine-singular
         </span>
         ") -
         <i>
          felices
         </i>
         ("happy-
         <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
          feminine-plural
         </span>
         ")
         <br/>
         <i>
          caço
         </i>
         ("I hunt") -
         <i>
          caces
         </i>
         ("you hunt")
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th rowspan="2">
         <i>
          g
         </i>
        </th>
        <td>
         /ʒ/ before
         <i>
          e
         </i>
         and
         <i>
          i
         </i>
         <br/>
         corresponds to
         <i>
          j
         </i>
         in other positions
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          envejar
         </i>
         ("to envy") -
         <i>
          envegen
         </i>
         ("they envy")
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         final
         <i>
          g
         </i>
         + stressed
         <i>
          i
         </i>
         , and final
         <i>
          ig
         </i>
         before other vowels,
         <br/>
         are pronounced [tʃ]
         <br/>
         corresponds to
         <i>
          j
         </i>
         ~
         <i>
          g
         </i>
         or
         <i>
          tj
         </i>
         ~
         <i>
          tg
         </i>
         in other positions
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          boig
         </i>
         ['bɔtʃ] ("mad-
         <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
          masculine
         </span>
         ") - boja ['bɔʒə] ("mad-
         <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
          feminine
         </span>
         ") - boges ['bɔʒəs] ("mad-
         <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
          feminine plural
         </span>
         ")
         <br/>
         <i>
          desig
         </i>
         [də'zitʃ] ("wish") -
         <i>
          desitjar
         </i>
         ("to wish") -
         <i>
          desitgem
         </i>
         ("we wish")
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th>
         <i>
          gu
         </i>
        </th>
        <td>
         /ɡ/ before
         <i>
          e
         </i>
         and
         <i>
          i
         </i>
         <br/>
         corresponds to
         <i>
          g
         </i>
         in other positions
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          botiga
         </i>
         ("shop") -
         <i>
          botigues
         </i>
         ("shops")
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th>
         <i>
          gü
         </i>
        </th>
        <td>
         /ɡw/ before
         <i>
          e
         </i>
         and
         <i>
          i
         </i>
         <br/>
         corresponds to
         <i>
          gu
         </i>
         in other positions
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          llengua
         </i>
         ("language") -
         <i>
          llengües
         </i>
         ("languages")
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th>
         <i>
          qu
         </i>
        </th>
        <td>
         /k/ before
         <i>
          e
         </i>
         and
         <i>
          i
         </i>
         <br/>
         corresponds to
         <i>
          q
         </i>
         in other positions
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          vaca
         </i>
         ("cow") -
         <i>
          vaques
         </i>
         ("cows")
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th>
         <i>
          qü
         </i>
        </th>
        <td>
         /kw/ before
         <i>
          e
         </i>
         and
         <i>
          i
         </i>
         <br/>
         corresponds to
         <i>
          qu
         </i>
         in other positions
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          obliqua
         </i>
         ("oblique-
         <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
          feminine
         </span>
         ") -
         <i>
          obliqües
         </i>
         ("oblique-
         <span class="smallcaps" style="font-variant:small-caps;">
          feminine plural
         </span>
         ")
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th>
         <i>
          x
         </i>
        </th>
        <td>
         [ʃ]~[tʃ] initially and in onsets after a consonant
         <br/>
         [ʃ] after
         <i>
          i
         </i>
         <br/>
         otherwise, [ɡz] before stress, [ks] after
        </td>
        <td>
         <i>
          xarxa
         </i>
         [ˈʃarʃə] ("net")
         <br/>
         <i>
          guix
         </i>
         [ˈɡiʃ] ("chalk")
         <br/>
         <i>
          exacte
         </i>
         [əɡˈzaktə] ("exact"),
         <i>
          fax
         </i>
         [ˈfaks] ("fax")
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Grammar">
        Grammar
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Grammar">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_grammar" title="Catalan grammar">
        Catalan grammar
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The grammar of Catalan is similar to other
       <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">
        Romance languages
       </a>
       . Features include:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESwan200197–98_102-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESwan200197–98-102">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Use of
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Definite_article" title="Definite article">
         definite
        </a>
        and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indefinite_article" title="Indefinite article">
         indefinite articles
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESwan200197–98_102-1">
         <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESwan200197–98-102">
          [102]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Noun" title="Noun">
         Nouns
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Adjective" title="Adjective">
         adjectives
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Pronoun" title="Pronoun">
         pronouns
        </a>
        , and
        <a href="/wiki/Article_(grammar)" title="Article (grammar)">
         articles
        </a>
        are
        <a href="/wiki/Inflection" title="Inflection">
         inflected
        </a>
        for
        <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_gender" title="Grammatical gender">
         gender
        </a>
        (masculine and feminine), and
        <a href="/wiki/Grammatical_number" title="Grammatical number">
         number
        </a>
        (singular and plural). There is no
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Case_(grammar)" title="Case (grammar)">
         case
        </a>
        inflexion, except in pronouns.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESwan200197–98_102-2">
         <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESwan200197–98-102">
          [102]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Verb" title="Verb">
         Verbs
        </a>
        are highly inflected for
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Person_(grammar)" title="Person (grammar)">
         person
        </a>
        ,
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Number_(grammar)" title="Number (grammar)">
         number
        </a>
        ,
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tense_(grammar)" title="Tense (grammar)">
         tense
        </a>
        ,
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aspect_(grammar)" title="Aspect (grammar)">
         aspect
        </a>
        , and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mood_(grammar)" title="Mood (grammar)">
         mood
        </a>
        (including a
        <a href="/wiki/Subjunctive_mood" title="Subjunctive mood">
         subjunctive
        </a>
        ).
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESwan200197–98_102-3">
         <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESwan200197–98-102">
          [102]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        There are no
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modal_auxiliary" title="Modal auxiliary">
         modal auxiliaries
        </a>
        .
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESwan200197–98_102-4">
         <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESwan200197–98-102">
          [102]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        Word order is freer than in English.
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESwan200197–98_102-5">
         <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESwan200197–98-102">
          [102]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Gender_and_number_inflection">
        Gender and number inflection
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Gender and number inflection">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flexi%C3%B3_of_word_Gat.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2392" data-file-width="920" height="390" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Flexi%C3%B3_of_word_Gat.jpg/150px-Flexi%C3%B3_of_word_Gat.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Flexi%C3%B3_of_word_Gat.jpg/225px-Flexi%C3%B3_of_word_Gat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Flexi%C3%B3_of_word_Gat.jpg/300px-Flexi%C3%B3_of_word_Gat.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flexi%C3%B3_of_word_Gat.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Gender and number inflection of the word
         <i>
          gat
         </i>
         ("cat")
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <table>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center;">
          <caption>
           Regular noun with definite article:
           <i>
            el gat
           </i>
           ("the cat")
          </caption>
          <tr>
           <th>
           </th>
           <th>
            masculine
           </th>
           <th>
            feminine
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <th>
            singular
           </th>
           <td>
            <i>
             el gat
            </i>
           </td>
           <td>
            <i>
             la gat
             <b>
              a
             </b>
            </i>
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <th>
            plural
           </th>
           <td>
            <i>
             els gat
             <b>
              s
             </b>
            </i>
           </td>
           <td>
            <i>
             les gat
             <b>
              es
             </b>
            </i>
           </td>
          </tr>
         </table>
        </td>
        <td>
         <table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center;">
          <caption>
           Adjective with 4 forms:
           <br/>
           <i>
            verd
           </i>
           ("green")
          </caption>
          <tr>
           <th>
           </th>
           <th>
            masculine
           </th>
           <th>
            feminine
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <th>
            singular
           </th>
           <td>
            <i>
             verd
            </i>
           </td>
           <td>
            <i>
             verd
             <b>
              a
             </b>
            </i>
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <th>
            plural
           </th>
           <td>
            <i>
             verd
             <b>
              s
             </b>
            </i>
           </td>
           <td>
            <i>
             verd
             <b>
              es
             </b>
            </i>
           </td>
          </tr>
         </table>
        </td>
        <td>
         <table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center;">
          <caption>
           Adjective with 3 forms:
           <br/>
           <i>
            feliç
           </i>
           ("happy")
          </caption>
          <tr>
           <th>
           </th>
           <th>
            masculine
           </th>
           <th>
            feminine
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <th>
            singular
           </th>
           <td colspan="2">
            <i>
             feliç
            </i>
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <th>
            plural
           </th>
           <td>
            <i>
             feliç
             <b>
              os
             </b>
            </i>
           </td>
           <td>
            <i>
             felic
             <b>
              es
             </b>
            </i>
           </td>
          </tr>
         </table>
        </td>
        <td>
         <table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center;">
          <caption>
           Adjective with 2 forms:
           <br/>
           <i>
            indiferent
           </i>
           ("indifferent")
          </caption>
          <tr>
           <th>
           </th>
           <th>
            masculine
           </th>
           <th>
            feminine
           </th>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <th>
            singular
           </th>
           <td colspan="2">
            <i>
             indiferent
            </i>
           </td>
          </tr>
          <tr>
           <th>
            plural
           </th>
           <td colspan="2">
            <i>
             indiferent
             <b>
              s
             </b>
            </i>
           </td>
          </tr>
         </table>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       In
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gender_inflection" title="Gender inflection">
        gender inflection
       </a>
       , the most notable feature is (compared to
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">
        Italian
       </a>
       ), the loss of the typical
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Masculine" title="Masculine">
        masculine
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Suffix" title="Suffix">
        suffix
       </a>
       <i>
        -o
       </i>
       . Thus, the alternance of
       <i>
        -o
       </i>
       /
       <i>
        -a
       </i>
       , has been replaced by
       <i>
        ø
       </i>
       /
       <i>
        -a
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630_52-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are only a few exceptions, like
       <i>
        minso
       </i>
       /
       <i>
        minsa
       </i>
       ("scarce").
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630_52-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Many not completely predictable morphological alternations may occur, such as:
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630_52-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Affrication:
        <i>
         bo
         <b>
          ig
         </b>
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         bo
         <b>
          j
         </b>
         <u>
          a
         </u>
        </i>
        ("insane") vs.
        <i>
         lle
         <b>
          ig
         </b>
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         lle
         <b>
          tj
         </b>
         <u>
          a
         </u>
        </i>
        ("ugly")
       </li>
       <li>
        Loss of
        <i>
         n
        </i>
        :
        <i>
         pla
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         pla
         <b>
          n
         </b>
         <u>
          a
         </u>
        </i>
        ("flat") vs.
        <i>
         sego
         <b>
          n
         </b>
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         sego
         <b>
          n
         </b>
         <u>
          a
         </u>
        </i>
        ("second")
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Final_obstruent_devoicing" title="Final obstruent devoicing">
         Final obstruent devoicing
        </a>
        :
        <i>
         senti
         <b>
          t
         </b>
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         senti
         <b>
          d
         </b>
         <u>
          a
         </u>
        </i>
        ("felt") vs.
        <i>
         di
         <b>
          t
         </b>
        </i>
        /
        <i>
         di
         <b>
          t
         </b>
         <u>
          a
         </u>
        </i>
        ("said")
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Catalan has few
       <a href="/wiki/Suppletion" title="Suppletion">
        suppletive
       </a>
       couplets, like Italian and Spanish, and unlike French. Thus, Catalan has
       <i>
        noi
       </i>
       /
       <i>
        noia
       </i>
       ("boy"/"girl") and
       <i>
        gall
       </i>
       /
       <i>
        gallina
       </i>
       ("cock"/"hen"), whereas French has
       <i>
        garçon
       </i>
       /
       <i>
        fille
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        coq
       </i>
       /
       <i>
        poule
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630_52-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       There is a tendency to abandon traditionally gender-invariable adjectives in favour of marked ones, something prevalent in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Occitan" title="Occitan">
        Occitan
       </a>
       and French. Thus, one can find
       <i>
        bullent
       </i>
       /
       <i>
        bullenta
       </i>
       ("boiling") in contrast with traditional
       <i>
        bullent
       </i>
       /
       <i>
        bullent
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630_52-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As in the other Western Romance languages, the main plural expression is the suffix
       <i>
        -s
       </i>
       , which may create morphological alternations similar to the ones found in gender inflection, albeit more rarely.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630_52-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The most important one is the addition of
       <i>
        -o-
       </i>
       before certain consonant groups, a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phonetic" title="Phonetic">
        phonetic
       </a>
       phenomenon that does not affect feminine forms:
       <i>
        el pols
       </i>
       /
       <i>
        els polsos
       </i>
       ("the pulse"/"the pulses") vs.
       <i>
        la pols
       </i>
       /
       <i>
        les pols
       </i>
       ("the dust"/"the dusts").
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630–631_103-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana630–631-103">
         [103]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Determiners">
        Determiners
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Determiners">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Begur_-_Pla%C3%A7a_de_la_Vila_-_Catalunya.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1213" data-file-width="1617" height="113" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Begur_-_Pla%C3%A7a_de_la_Vila_-_Catalunya.jpg/150px-Begur_-_Pla%C3%A7a_de_la_Vila_-_Catalunya.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Begur_-_Pla%C3%A7a_de_la_Vila_-_Catalunya.jpg/225px-Begur_-_Pla%C3%A7a_de_la_Vila_-_Catalunya.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Begur_-_Pla%C3%A7a_de_la_Vila_-_Catalunya.jpg/300px-Begur_-_Pla%C3%A7a_de_la_Vila_-_Catalunya.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Begur_-_Pla%C3%A7a_de_la_Vila_-_Catalunya.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Sign in the town square of
         <a href="/wiki/Begur,_Spain" title="Begur, Spain">
          Begur
         </a>
         , Catalonia, Spain. In
         <i>
          Plaça de la vila
         </i>
         (literally "square of the town"), since the noun
         <i>
          vila
         </i>
         ("town") is feminine singular, the definite article carries the corresponding form,
         <i>
          la
         </i>
         ("the").
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>

      <p>
       The inflection of determinatives is complex, specially because of the high number of elisions, but is similar to the neighboring languages.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631_99-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Catalan has more contractions of preposition + article than
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       , like
       <i>
        dels
       </i>
       ("of + the [plural]"), but not as many as
       <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">
        Italian
       </a>
       (which has
       <i>
        sul
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        col
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        nel
       </i>
       , etc.).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631_99-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Central Catalan has abandoned almost completely unstressed possessives (
       <i>
        mon
       </i>
       , etc.) in favour of constructions of article + stressed forms (
       <i>
        el meu
       </i>
       , etc.), a feature shared with Italian.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631_99-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>

       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">

        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center; float:right;">

      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_personal_pronouns" title="Catalan personal pronouns">
        Catalan personal pronouns
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The morphology of Catalan personal pronouns is complex, specially in unstressed forms, which are numerous (13 distinct forms, compared to 11 in Spanish or 9 in Italian).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631_99-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Features include the gender-neutral
       <i>
        ho
       </i>
       and the great degree of freedom when combining different unstressed pronouns (65 combinations).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631_99-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Catalan pronouns exhibit
       <a href="/wiki/T%E2%80%93V_distinction" title="T–V distinction">
        T–V distinction
       </a>
       , like all other Romance languages (and most European languages, but not Modern English). This feature implies the use of a different set of second person pronouns for formality.
      </p>
      <p>
       This flexibility allows Catalan to use
       <a href="/wiki/Extraposition" title="Extraposition">
        extraposition
       </a>
       extensively, much more than French or Spanish. Thus, Catalan can have
       <i>
        m'hi recomanaren
       </i>
       ("they recommended me to him"), whereas in French one must say
       <i>
        ils m'ont recommandé à lui
       </i>
       , and Spanish
       <i>
        me recomendaron a él
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631_99-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This allows the placement of almost any nominal term as a sentence
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Topic%E2%80%93comment" title="Topic–comment">
        topic
       </a>
       , without having to use so often the
       <a href="/wiki/Passive_voice" title="Passive voice">
        passive voice
       </a>
       (as in French or
       <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">
        English
       </a>
       ), or identifying the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Direct_object" title="Direct object">
        direct object
       </a>
       with a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Preposition" title="Preposition">
        preposition
       </a>
       (as in Spanish).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631_99-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div style="clear:both;">
      </div>

      <p>
       Like all the Romance languages, Catalan verbal inflection is more complex than the nominal.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suffixation" title="Suffixation">
        Suffixation
       </a>
       is omnipresent, whereas morphological alternations play a secondary role.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631_99-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Vowel alternances are active, as well as infixation and suppletion. However, these are not as productive as in Spanish, and are mostly restricted to irregular verbs.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631_99-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Catalan verbal system is basically common to all Western Romance, except that most dialects have replaced the synthetic indicative perfect with a periphrastic form of
       <i>
        anar
       </i>
       ("to go") + infinitive.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631_99-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Catalan verbs are traditionally divided into three conjugations, with vowel themes
       <i>
        -a-
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        -e-
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        -i-
       </i>
       , the last two being split into two subtypes. However, this division is mostly theoretical.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631_99-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Only the first conjugation is nowadays productive (with about 3500 common verbs), whereas the third (the subtype of
       <i>
        servir
       </i>
       , with about 700 common verbs) is semiproductive. The verbs of the second conjugation are fewer than 100, and it is not possible to create new ones, except by compounding.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631_99-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEEnciclopèdia_Catalana631-99">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div style="clear:both;">
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Syntax">
        Syntax
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Syntax">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_syntax" title="Catalan syntax">
        Catalan syntax
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The grammar of Catalan follows the general pattern of Western Romance languages. The primary
       <a href="/wiki/Word_order" title="Word order">
        word order
       </a>
       is
       <a href="/wiki/Subject%E2%80%93verb%E2%80%93object" title="Subject–verb–object">
        subject–verb–object
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
        <a href="#cite_note-108">
         [108]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, word order is very flexible. Commonly, verb-subject constructions are used to achieve a semantic effect. The sentence "The train has arrived" could be translated as "Ha arribat el tren" or "El tren ha arribat." Both sentences mean "the train has arrived", but the former puts a focus on the train, while the latter puts a focus on the arrival. This subtle distinction is described as "what you might say while waiting in the station" versus "what you might say on the train."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WheelerYatesDols_109-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-WheelerYatesDols-109">
         [109]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Catalan_names">
        Catalan names
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Catalan names">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catalan_names" title="Catalan names">
        Catalan names
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">
        Spain
       </a>
       , every person officially has two surnames, one of which is the father's first surname and the other is the mother's first surname.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler20058_110-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler20058-110">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The law contemplates the possibility of joining both surnames with the Catalan conjunction
       <i>
        i
       </i>
       ("and").
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEWheeler20058_110-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEWheeler20058-110">
         [110]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
        <a href="#cite_note-111">
         [111]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sample_text">
        Sample text
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Catalan_language&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Sample text">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Selected text
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESwan2001112_112-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESwan2001112-112">
         [112]
        </a>
       </sup>
       from
       <a href="/wiki/Manuel_de_Pedrolo" title="Manuel de Pedrolo">
        Manuel de Pedrolo
       </a>
       's 1970 novel
       <i>
        Un amor fora ciutat
       </i>
       ("A love affair outside the city").
      </p>
      <table border="0" style="width:100%; text-align:left;">
       <tr>
        <td>
         <b>
          Original
         </b>
        </td>
        <td>
         <small>
          <b>
           Word-for-word translation
          </b>
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTESwan2001112_112-1">
           <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTESwan2001112-112">
            [112]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </small>
        </td>
        <td>
         <b>
          Free translation
         </b>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <i>
          Tenia prop de divuit anys quan vaig conèxier
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <small>
          I was having close to eighteen years, when I go [past auxiliary] know (=I met)
         </small>
        </td>
        <td>
         I was about eighteen years old when I met
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <i>
          en Raül, a l'estació de
          <a href="/wiki/Manresa" title="Manresa">
           Manresa
          </a>
          .
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <small>
          the Raül, at the station of (=in) Manresa.
         </small>
        </td>
        <td>
         Raül, at
         <a href="/wiki/Manresa" title="Manresa">
          Manresa
         </a>
         railway station.
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <i>
          El meu pare havia mort, inesperadament i encara jove,
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <small>
          The my father had died, unexpectedly and still young,
         </small>
        </td>
        <td>
         My father had died, unexpectedly and still young,
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <i>
          un parell d'anys abans, i d'aquells temps
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <small>
          a couple of years before, and of those times
         </small>
        </td>
        <td>
         a couple of years before; and from that time
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <i>
          conservo un record de punyent solitud.
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <small>
          I keep a memory of acute loneliness
         </small>
        </td>
        <td>
         I still harbour memories of great loneliness.
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <i>
          Les meves relacions amb la mare
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <small>
          The my relations with the mother
         </small>
        </td>
        <td>
         My relationship with my mother
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <i>
          no havien pas millorat, tot el contrari,
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <small>
          not had at all improved, all the contrary,
         </small>
        </td>
        <td>
         had not improved; quite the contrary,
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <i>
          potser fins i tot empitjoraven
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <small>
          perhaps even they were worsening
         </small>
        </td>
        <td>
         and arguably it was getting even worse
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <i>
          a mesura que em feia gran.
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <small>
          at step that (=in proportion as) myself I was making big (=I was growing up).
         </small>
        </td>
        <td>
         as I grew up.
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <i>
          No existia, no existí mai entre nosaltres,
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <small>
          Not it was existing, not it existed never between us,
         </small>
        </td>
        <td>
         There did not exist, at no point had there ever existed between us
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <i>
          una comunitat d'interessos, d'afeccions.
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <small>
          a community of interests, of affections.
         </small>
        </td>
        <td>
         shared interests or affection.
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <i>
          Cal creure que cercava... una persona
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <small>
          It is necessary to believe that I was seeking... a person
         </small>
        </td>
        <td>
         I guess I was seeking... a person
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td>
         <i>
          en qui centrar la meva vida afectiva.
         </i>
        </td>
        <td>
         <small>
          in whom to center the my life affective.
         </small>
        </td>
        <td>
         in whom I could center my emotional life.
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>

           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMoll195847_37-4">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              e
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <a href="#CITEREFMoll1958">
           Moll 1958
          </a>
          , p. 47.
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-e18-38">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          ^
          <a href="#cite_ref-e18_38-0">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              a
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-e18_38-1">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              b
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
         </span>
         <span class="error mw-ext-cite-error" dir="ltr" lang="en">

          <code>

         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-estiagem-39">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          ^
          <a href="#cite_ref-estiagem_39-0">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              a
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-estiagem_39-1">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              b
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          Portuguese and Spanish have
          <i>
           estiagem
          </i>
          and
          <i>
           estiaje
          </i>
          , respectively, for drought, dry season or low water levels.
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-vespera-40">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          ^
          <a href="#cite_ref-vespera_40-0">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              a
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
          <a href="#cite_ref-vespera_40-1">
           <sup>
            <i>
             <b>
              b
             </b>
            </i>
           </sup>
          </a>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          Portuguese and Spanish have
          <i>
           véspera
          </i>
          and
          <i>
           víspera
          </i>
          , respectively, for eve, or the day before.
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-trozo-41">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-trozo_41-0">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          Spanish also has
          <i>
           trozo
          </i>
          , and it is actually a borrowing from Catalan
          <i>
           tros
          </i>
          . Colón 1993, p 39. Portuguese has
          <i>
           troço
          </i>
          , but aside from also being a loanword, it has a very different meaning: "thing", "gadget", "tool", "paraphernalia".
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-42">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-42">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          Modern Spanish also has
          <i>
           gris,
          </i>
          but it is a modern borrowing from Occitan. The original word was
          <i>
           pardo
          </i>
          , which stands for "reddish, yellow-orange, medium-dark and of moderate to weak saturation. It also can mean ochre, pale ochre, dark ohre, brownish, tan, greyish, grey, desaturated, dirty, dark, or opaque."
          <cite class="citation book">
           Gallego, Rosa; Sanz, Juan Carlos (2001).
           <i>
            Diccionario Akal del color
           </i>
           (in Spanish). Akal.
           <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
            ISBN
           </a>
           <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-84-460-1083-8" title="Special:BookSources/978-84-460-1083-8">
            978-84-460-1083-8
           </a>
           .
          </cite>

           <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
            ISBN
           </a>
           <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-84-344-2884-3" title="Special:BookSources/978-84-344-2884-3">
            978-84-344-2884-3
           </a>
           .
          </cite>
          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=De+la+fon%C3%A8tica+a+la+fonologia%3A+les+consonants+i+assimilacions+conson%C3%A0ntiques+del+catal%C3%A0&amp;rft.place=Barcelona&amp;rft.pub=Editorial+Ariel&amp;rft.date=2001&amp;rft.isbn=978-84-344-2884-3&amp;rft.aulast=Recasens&amp;rft.aufirst=Daniel&amp;rft.au=Pallar%C3%A8s%2C+Maria+Dolors&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACatalan+language">

          . Here the authors label these Catalan sounds as "laminal postalveolar"

         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAcadèmia_Valenciana_de_la_Llengua2005_94-0">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>

        <li id="cite_note-95">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-95">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          Original full text of Dictamen 1:
          <i>
           D’acord amb les aportacions més solvents de la romanística acumulades des del segle XIX fins a l’actualitat (estudis de gramàtica històrica, de dialectologia, de sintaxi, de lexicografia…), la llengua pròpia i històrica dels valencians, des del punt de vista de la filologia, és també la que compartixen les comunitats autònomes de Catalunya i de les Illes Balears i el Principat d’Andorra. Així mateix és la llengua històrica i pròpia d’altres territoris de l’antiga Corona d’Aragó (la franja oriental aragonesa, la ciutat sarda de l’Alguer i el departament francés dels Pirineus Orientals). Els diferents parlars de tots estos territoris constituïxen una llengua, és a dir, un mateix «sistema lingüístic», segons la terminologia del primer estructuralisme (annex 1) represa en el Dictamen del Consell Valencià de Cultura, que figura com a preàmbul de la Llei de Creació de l’AVL. Dins d’eixe conjunt de parlars, el valencià té la mateixa jerarquia i dignitat que qualsevol altra modalitat territorial del sistema lingüístic, i presenta unes característiques pròpies que l’AVL preservarà i potenciarà d’acord amb la tradició lexicogràfica i literària pròpia, la realitat lingüística valenciana i la normativització consolidada a partir de les Normes de Castelló.
          </i>
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-96">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-96">
            ^
           </a>

         <span class="reference-text">
          <a class="external text" href="http://www.lavanguardia.mobi/slowdevice/noticia/51262801790/Casi-el-65-de-los-valencianos-opina-que-su-lengua-es-distinta-al-catalan-segun-una-encuesta-del-CIS.html" rel="nofollow">
           Casi el 65% de los valencianos opina que su lengua es distinta al catalán, según una encuesta del CIS
          </a>
         </span>
        </li>

        <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=Catalan&amp;rft.btitle=Concise+Encyclopedia+of+Languages+of+the+World&amp;rft.place=Oxford&amp;rft.pages=188-192&amp;rft.pub=Elsevier&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-08-087774-7&amp;rft.aulast=Wheeler&amp;rft.aufirst=Max&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2F%3Fid%3DF2SRqDzB50wC%26printsec%3Dfrontcover%23v%3Donepage%26q%26f%3Dfalse&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACatalan+language">
         <span style="display:none;">
         </span>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        <cite class="citation book" id="CITEREFVeny1997">
         Veny, Joan (1997). "greuges de Guitard isarn, Senyor de Caboet (1080–1095)".
         <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/?id=OMaXD1caTiEC&amp;pg=PA17&amp;dq=greuges+guitard+isarn#v=onepage&amp;q=greuges%20guitard%20isarn&amp;f=false" rel="nofollow">
          <i>
           Homenatge a Arthur Terry
          </i>
         </a>
         . Barcelona: Publicacions de l'Abadia de Montserrat. pp. 9–18.
         <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
          ISBN

         <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/84-7826-894-4" title="Special:BookSources/84-7826-894-4">

         </a>

        </cite>
        <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.atitle=greuges+de+Guitard+isarn%2C+Senyor+de+Caboet+%281080%E2%80%931095%29&amp;rft.btitle=Homenatge+a+Arthur+Terry&amp;rft.place=Barcelona&amp;rft.pages=9-18&amp;rft.pub=Publicacions+de+l%27Abadia+de+Montserrat&amp;rft.date=1997&amp;rft.isbn=84-7826-894-4&amp;rft.aulast=Veny&amp;rft.aufirst=Joan&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2F%3Fid%3DOMaXD1caTiEC%26pg%3DPA17%26dq%3Dgreuges%2Bguitard%2Bisarn%23v%3Donepage%26q%3Dgreuges%2520guitard%2520isarn%26f%3Dfalse&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ACatalan+language">

       <b>
        About the Catalan language
       </b>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20110529085634/http://www2.iec.cat/institucio/seccions/Filologica/gramatica/default.asp" rel="nofollow">

        </a>
        (Catalan grammar)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="external text" href="http://www.verbs.cat/" rel="nofollow">
         verbs.cat
        </a>
        (Catalan verb conjugations with online trainers)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20121222153529/http://www.gereon.greenheart.es/catala.php?lan=en" rel="nofollow">
         Catalan and its dialects
        </a>
       </li>
      </ul>

      <p>
       <b>
        Automated translation systems
       </b>
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20070701132905/http://traductor.gencat.net/text.do" rel="nofollow">
         Traductor
        </a>
        automated, online translations of text and web pages (Catalan ↔ English, French and Spanish)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="external text" href="http://sishitra.iti.upv.es/" rel="nofollow">
         SisHiTra
        </a>
        automated, online translations of text and web pages (Catalan–Spanish)
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="external text" href="http://apertium.org" rel="nofollow">
         apertium.org
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Apertium" title="Apertium">
         Apertium
        </a>
        (
        <a href="/wiki/Free_software" title="Free software">
         free software
        </a>
        ) translates text, documents or web pages, online or offline, between Catalan and
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aranese" title="Aranese">
         Aranese
        </a>
        , English,
        <a href="/wiki/Esperanto" title="Esperanto">
         Esperanto
        </a>
        , French,
        <a href="/wiki/Occitan_language" title="Occitan language">
         Occitan
        </a>
        , Portuguese and Spanish
       </li>
       <li>
        <a class="external text" href="https://translate.google.com/translate_t?hl=&amp;ie=UTF-8&amp;text=frontera&amp;sl=ca&amp;tl=en#ca%7Cen" rel="nofollow">
         translate.google.com
        </a>
        online translations Catalan &lt;&gt; English and other languages
       </li>
      </ul>

               <div>
                <div class="hlist hlist-separated">
                 <ul>
                  <li>
                   <i>
                    Italics
                   </i>
                   indicate
                   <a href="/wiki/Language_death" title="Language death">
                    extinct languages
                   </a>
                  </li>
                  <li>
                   <b>
                    Bold
                   </b>
                   indicates
                   <a href="/wiki/List_of_languages_by_number_of_native_speakers" title="List of languages by number of native speakers">
                    languages with more than 5 million speakers
                   </a>
                  </li>
                  <li>
                   Languages between parentheses are
                   <a href="/wiki/Variety_(linguistics)" title="Variety (linguistics)">
                    varieties
                   </a>
                   of the language on their left.
                  </li>
                 </ul>
